1 S.30
3 8 V.S.A. chapter 107
4 It is hereby enacted by the General Assembly of the State of Vermont:
5 * * * Repeal of Existing 8 V.S.A. Chapter 107 * * *
6 Sec. 1. REPEAL OF EXISTING 8 V.S.A. CHAPTER 107
7 8 V.S.A. chapter 107 (health insurance) is repealed.
8 * * * Enactment of Updated and Reorganized 8 V.S.A. Chapter 107 * * *
9 Sec. 2. 8 V.S.A. chapter 107 is added to read:
10 CHAPTER 107. HEALTH INSURANCE
11 Subchapter 1. General Provisions
12 § 4011. DEFINITIONS
13 As used in this chapter:
14 (1) “Covered individual” means an individual who is covered by a
15 health insurance plan, whether as the primary subscriber or policyholder or as a
16 dependent, employee, or employee’s dependent under the plan.
17 (2) “Health care services” means services for the diagnosis, prevention,
18 treatment, cure, or relief of a health condition, illness, injury, or disease.
19 (3) “Health insurance plan” means a policy or contract issued by a
20 health insurer, including the health benefit plan or plans offered by the State of
21 Vermont to its employees and any health benefit plan offered by any agency or
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 2 of 181
1 instrumentality of the State to its employees. Unless otherwise specified,
2 “health insurance” does not include Vermont Medicaid.
3 (4) “Health insurer” means an insurance company that provides health
4 insurance as defined in subdivision 3301(a)(2) of this title, a nonprofit hospital
5 or medical service corporation, a managed care organization, a health
6 maintenance organization, and, to the extent permitted under federal law, any
7 administrator of an insured, self-insured, or publicly funded health care benefit
8 plan offered by a public or private entity.
9 (5) “Major medical insurance” means a comprehensive health insurance
10 plan that is not specific disease, accident, hospital indemnity, dental care,
11 vision care, disability income, long-term care, Medicare supplement insurance,
12 or other limited-benefit coverage. The term does not include short-term,
13 limited-duration health insurance coverage or a plan under which benefits are
14 paid directly to a covered individual or the individual’s assigns and for which
15 the amount of the benefit is not based on potential medical costs or on actual
16 costs incurred.
17 § 4012. COMPLIANCE WITH FEDERAL LAW
18 (a) Except as otherwise provided in this title, health insurers, hospital and
19 medical service corporations, and health maintenance organizations that issue,
20 sell, renew, or offer health insurance plans in Vermont shall comply with the
21 requirements of the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act of
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 3 of 181
1 1996, as amended from time to time (42 U.S.C. Chapter 6A, Subchapter
2 XXV), and the Patient Protection and Affordable Care Act of 2010, Pub. L.
3 No. 111-148, as amended by the Health Care and Education Reconciliation Act
4 of 2010, Pub. L. No. 111-152. The Commissioner shall enforce such
5 requirements pursuant to the Commissioner’s authority under this title.
6 (b)(1) Health insurers, hospital and medical service corporations, health
7 maintenance organizations, and health care providers, as that term is defined in
8 18 V.S.A. § 9432, shall comply with the requirements of the No Surprises Act,
9 Pub. L. No. 116-260, Division BB, Title I, as amended from time to time.
10 (2) The Commissioner shall enforce the requirements of the No
11 Surprises Act as they apply to health insurers, hospital and medical service
12 corporations, health maintenance organizations, and health care providers, to
13 the extent permitted under federal law, pursuant to the Commissioner’s
14 authority under this title. The Commissioner may also refer cases of
15 noncompliance to the U.S. Department of Health and Human Services under
16 the terms of a collaborative enforcement agreement, or to the Office of the
17 Vermont Attorney General.
18 § 4013. DISCRIMINATION PROHIBITED
19 No health insurer shall make or permit any unfair discrimination between
20 individuals of substantially the same hazard in the amount of premium rates
21 charged for any health insurance plan or in the benefits payable under the plan;
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 4 of 181
1 provided, however, that this section shall not be construed to prohibit different
2 premium rates, different benefits, or different underwriting procedure for
3 individuals insured under group, family expense, or blanket plans of insurance.
4 § 4014. ADVERTISING PRACTICES
5 (a) No company doing business in this State, and no insurance agent or
6 broker, shall use in connection with the solicitation of health insurance or
7 pharmacy benefit management any advertising copy or advertising practice or
8 any plan of solicitation that is materially misleading or deceptive. An
9 advertising copy or advertising practice or plan of solicitation shall be
10 considered to be materially misleading or deceptive if by implication or
11 otherwise it transmits information in such manner or of such substance that a
12 prospective applicant for health insurance may be misled by it to the
13 applicant’s material damage.
14 (b)(1) If the Commissioner finds that any such advertising copy or
15 advertising practice or plan of solicitation is materially misleading or
16 deceptive, the Commissioner shall order the company or the agent or broker
17 using such copy or practice or plan to cease and desist from such use.
18 (2) Before making any such finding and order, the Commissioner shall
19 give notice, not less than 10 days in advance, and a hearing to the company,
20 agent, or broker affected.
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 5 of 181
1 (3) If the Commissioner finds, after due notice and hearing, that any
2 authorized insurer, licensed pharmacy benefit manager, licensed insurance
3 agent, or licensed insurance broker has intentionally violated any such order to
4 cease and desist, the Commissioner may suspend or revoke the license of such
5 insurer, pharmacy benefit manager, agent, or broker.
6 § 4015. PENALTIES FOR VIOLATIONS
7 The Commissioner may impose an administrative penalty of up to $750.00
8 on any person who intentionally violates any provision of this chapter or any
9 order of the Commissioner made in accordance with this chapter. The
10 Commissioner may also suspend or revoke the license of a health insurer or
11 agent for any such intentional violation.
12 § 4016. APPEAL
13 (a) Any person aggrieved by any action of the Commissioner may obtain a
14 review by appeal to the Superior Court of Washington County. The appeal
15 shall be based on the record of the proceedings before the Commissioner and
16 shall not be limited to questions of law. If the appeal is from an order of the
17 Commissioner, the order shall not take effect during the pendency of the
18 appeal unless the court determines otherwise.
19 (b) The court may review all the facts and in disposing of any issue before
20 it may modify, affirm, or reverse any order of the Commissioner in whole or in
21 part.
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 6 of 181
1 (c) Either party may appeal from the decision of the Superior Court to the
2 Supreme Court in the manner provided by law.
3 § 4017. EXEMPTION FROM ATTACHMENT AND TRUSTEE PROCESS
4 So much of any benefits under all policies of health insurance as does not
5 exceed $200.00 for each month during any period of disability covered by the
6 policy shall not be liable to attachment, trustee process, or other process, or to
7 be seized, taken, appropriated, or applied by any legal or equitable process or
8 by operation of law, either before or after payment of such benefits, to pay any
9 debt or liabilities of the person insured under the policy. However, this
10 exemption shall not apply where an action is brought to recover for necessaries
11 contracted for during the period of disability and the writ or bill of complaint
12 contains a statement to that effect. When a policy provides for a lump sum
13 payment because of a dismemberment or other loss insured, the payment shall
14 be exempt from execution of the covered individual’s creditors.
15 § 4018. THIRD-PARTY OWNERSHIP
16 Nothing in this chapter shall be construed as preventing a person other than
17 the covered individual with proper insurable interest from making application
18 for and owning a policy covering the covered individual or from being entitled
19 under such a policy to any indemnities, benefits, and rights provided in the
20 policy.
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 7 of 181
1 § 4019. NOTICE AS WAIVER
2 A health insurer shall not be deemed to have waived any rights to defend a
3 claim under a health insurance plan based solely on the health insurer’s
4 acknowledgement of receipt of notice under the plan, furnishing or accepting
5 forms for filing proof of loss under the plan, or investigating any claim of loss
6 under the plan.
7 § 4020. AGE LIMITS
8 (a) If a health insurance plan contains a provision establishing, as an age
9 limit or otherwise, a date after which the coverage provided by the plan will
10 not be effective, and if that date falls within a period for which the health
11 insurer has accepted a premium or if the health insurer accepts a premium after
12 that date, the coverage provided by the plan shall continue in force subject to
13 any right of cancellation until the end of the period for which a premium has
14 been accepted.
15 (b) Notwithstanding any provision of subsection (a) of this section to the
16 contrary, if the age of the covered individual has been misstated and if,
17 according to the correct age of the covered individual, the coverage provided
18 by the policy would not have become effective or would have ceased prior to
19 the health insurer’s acceptance of the premium or premiums, then the health
20 insurer’s liability shall be limited to the refund, upon request, of all premiums
21 paid for the period not covered by the plan.
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 8 of 181
1 § 4021. TERMINATION OF COVERAGE
2 (a)(1) A major medical insurance policy issued by a health insurer that
3 insures employees, members, or subscribers for hospital and medical insurance
4 on an expense-incurred, service, or prepaid basis shall:
5 (A) provide notice to the policyholder or other responsible party of
6 any premium payment due on a policy at least 21 days before the due date; and
7 (B) provide a grace period of at least one month for the payment of
8 each premium falling due after the first premium, during which grace period
9 the plan shall continue in force and the issuer of the plan shall be liable for
10 valid claims for covered losses incurred prior to the end of the grace period.
11 (2) If the issuer of a plan described subdivision (1) of this subsection
12 does not receive payment by the due date, the issuer shall send a termination
13 notice to the policyholder at least 21 days prior to termination notifying the
14 policyholder that the issuer may terminate the plan if payment is not received
15 by the termination date.
16 (3) The termination date of a plan described in subdivision (1) of this
17 subsection shall not be earlier than the day following the last day of the grace
18 period set forth in subdivision (1)(A) of this subsection.
19 (b) For all health insurance policies other than major medical insurance
20 policies, a health insurer shall notify a policyholder of any premium payment
21 due on a policy at least 21 days before the due date. If a health insurer does
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 9 of 181
1 not receive payment by the due date, the health insurer shall send a termination
2 notice to the policyholder notifying the policyholder that the health insurer will
3 terminate the policy effective on the due date if payment is not received within
4 14 days from the date of mailing of the termination notice. If a health insurer
5 does not receive payment within 14 days from the date of mailing of the
6 termination notice, the health insurer may cancel coverage effective on the due
7 date.
8 § 4022. REBATES AND COMMISSIONS PROHIBITED FOR NONGROUP
9 AND SMALL GROUP POLICIES AND PLANS OFFERED
10 THROUGH THE VERMONT HEALTH BENEFIT EXCHANGE
11 (a) No health insurer doing business in this State and no insurance agent or
12 broker shall:
13 (1) offer, promise, allow, give, set off, or pay, directly or indirectly:
14 (A) any rebate of or part of the premium payable on a health
15 insurance plan issued pursuant to 33 V.S.A. § 1811 or earnings, profits,
16 dividends, or other benefits founded, arising, accruing, or to accrue on or from
17 the premium;
18 (B) any special advantage in date of policy or age of issue;
19 (C) any paid employment or contract for services of any kind;
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 10 of 181
1 (D) any other valuable consideration or inducement to or for
2 insurance on any risk in this State, or for or upon any renewal of any such
3 insurance, that is not specified in the health insurance plan; or
4 (2) offer, promise, give, option, sell, or purchase any stocks, bonds,
5 securities, or property, or any dividends or profits accruing or to accrue on
6 them, or other thing of value as inducement to insurance or in connection with
7 insurance, or any renewal thereof, that is not specified in the health insurance
8 plan.
9 (b) No person insured under a health insurance plan issued pursuant to
10 33 V.S.A. § 1811 or party or applicant for such plan shall directly or indirectly
11 receive or accept or agree to receive or accept any rebate of premium or of any
12 part of the premium, or any favor or advantage, or share in any benefit to
13 accrue under any health insurance plan issued pursuant 33 V.S.A. § 1811, or
14 any valuable consideration or inducement, that is not specified in the health
15 insurance plan.
16 (c) Nothing in this section shall be construed as prohibiting any health
17 insurer from:
18 (1) allowing or returning to its participating policyholders dividends,
19 savings, or unused premium deposits;
20 (2) returning or otherwise abating, in full or in part, the premiums of its
21 policyholders out of surplus accumulated from nonparticipating insurance; or
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 11 of 181
1 (3) taking a bona fide obligation, with interest not exceeding six percent
2 per annum, in payment of any premium.
3 (d)(1) No insurer shall pay any commission, fee, or other compensation,
4 directly or indirectly, to a licensed or unlicensed agent, broker, or other
5 individual in connection with the sale of a health insurance plan issued
6 pursuant to 33 V.S.A. § 1811, nor shall a health insurer include in an insurance
7 rate for a health insurance plan issued pursuant to 33 V.S.A. § 1811 any sums
8 related to services provided by an agent, broker, or other individual. A health
9 insurer may provide to its employees wages, salary, and other employment-
10 related compensation in connection with the sale of health insurance plans, but
11 shall not structure any such compensation in a manner that promotes the sale of
12 particular health insurance plans over other plans offered by that insurer.
13 (2) Nothing in this subsection shall be construed to prohibit the Vermont
14 Health Benefit Exchange established in 33 V.S.A. chapter 18, subchapter 1
15 from structuring compensation for agents or brokers in the form of an
16 additional commission, fee, or other compensation outside insurance rates or
17 from compensating agents, brokers, or other individuals through the
18 procedures and payment mechanisms established pursuant to 33 V.S.A.
19 § 1805(17).

1 § 4022a. REBATES PROHIBITED FOR GROUP INSURANCE POLICIES
2 (a) As used in this section, “group insurance” means any policy described
3 in section 4041 of this title, except that it shall not include any small group
4 policy issued pursuant to 33 V.S.A. § 1811.
5 (b) No health insurer doing business in this State and no insurance agent or
6 broker shall:
7 (1) offer, promise, allow, give, set off, or pay, directly or indirectly:
8 (A) any rebate of or part of the premium payable on a group
9 insurance policy, or on any group insurance policy or agent’s commission on
10 the premium or earnings, profits, dividends, or other benefits founded, arising,
11 accruing, or to accrue on or from the premium;
12 (B) any special advantage in date of policy or age of issue;
13 (C) any paid employment or contract for services of any kind; or
14 (D) any other valuable consideration or inducement to or for
15 insurance on any risk in this State, or for or upon any renewal of any such
16 insurance, that is not specified in the health insurance plan; or
17 (2) offer, promise, give, option, sell, or purchase any stocks, bonds,
18 securities, or property, or any dividends or profits accruing or to accrue on
19 them, or other thing of value as inducement to insurance or in connection with
20 insurance, or any renewal thereof, that is not specified in the health insurance
21 plan.

3 § 4023. PROVISIONS APPLYING TO POLICIES DELIVERED IN
4 ANOTHER STATE
5 If any policy is issued by a health insurer domiciled in this State for
6 delivery to a person residing in another state, and if the official having
7 responsibility for the administration of the insurance laws of the other state
8 informs the Commissioner that the policy is not subject to approval or
9 disapproval by the official, the Commissioner may issue an order requiring that
10 the policy meet the standards set forth in sections 4029, 4030, and 4031 of this
11 title.
12 § 4024. COORDINATION OF INSURANCE COVERAGE WITH
13 MEDICAID AND COMPLIANCE WITH MEDICAID RECOVERY
14 PROVISIONS
15 (a) No health insurer shall consider the availability of or eligibility for
16 medical assistance in this or any other state under Title XIX of the Social
17 Security Act (Medicaid) when considering eligibility for coverage or making
18 payments under its plan for eligible enrollees, subscribers, policyholders, or
19 certificate holders.
20 (b) A health insurer that issues, sells, renews, or offers health insurance
21 coverage in Vermont or who is required to be licensed or registered with the
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 15 of 181
1 Department shall comply with the requirements of 33 V.S.A. §§ 1907, 1908,
2 1909, and 1910. The Commissioner shall enforce such requirements pursuant
3 to the Commissioner’s authority under this title.
4 § 4025. HEALTH INSURANCE AND THE BLUEPRINT FOR HEALTH
5 (a) All major medical insurance plans shall be offered, issued, and
6 administered consistent with the Blueprint for Health established in 18 V.S.A.
7 chapter 13.
8 (b) Health insurers offering major medical insurance plans shall participate
9 in the Blueprint for Health as specified in 18 V.S.A. § 706.
10 Subchapter 2. Policy Forms and Filing Requirements
11 § 4026. FILING AND APPROVAL OF POLICY FORMS AND PREMIUMS
12 (a)(1) No policy of health insurance or certificate under a policy filed by a
13 health insurer and not exempted by subdivision 3368(a)(4) of this title shall be
14 delivered or issued for delivery in this State, nor shall any endorsement, rider,
15 or application that becomes a part of any such policy be used, until a copy of
16 the form and of the rules for the classification of risks has been filed with the
17 Department of Financial Regulation and a copy of the premium rates has been
18 filed with the Green Mountain Care Board, and the Green Mountain Care
19 Board has issued a decision approving, modifying, or disapproving the
20 proposed rate.

1 (2)(A) The Green Mountain Care Board shall review rate requests and
2 shall approve, modify, or disapprove a rate request within 90 calendar days
3 after receipt of an initial rate filing from a health insurer. If a health insurer
4 fails to provide necessary materials or other information to the Board in a
5 timely manner, the Board may extend its review for a reasonable additional
6 period of time, not to exceed 30 calendar days.
7 (B) Prior to the Board’s decision on a rate request, the Department of
8 Financial Regulation shall provide the Board with an analysis and opinion on
9 the impact of the proposed rate on the insurer’s solvency and reserves.
10 (3) The Board shall determine whether a rate is affordable; promotes
11 quality care; promotes access to health care; protects insurer solvency; and is
12 not unjust, unfair, inequitable, misleading, or contrary to the laws of this State.
13 In making this determination, the Board shall consider the analysis and opinion
14 provided by the Department of Financial Regulation pursuant to subdivision
15 (2)(B) of this subsection.
16 (b)(1) In conjunction with a rate filing required by subsection (a) of this
17 section, a health insurer shall file a plain language summary of the proposed
18 rate. All summaries shall include a brief justification of any rate increase
19 requested, the information that the Secretary of the U.S. Department of Health
20 and Human Services (HHS) requires for rate increases over 10 percent, and
21 any other information required by the Board. The plain language summary

5 not apply to the policy forms for major medical insurance coverage or to the
6 rate and policy form review process for policies for specific disease, accident,
7 injury, hospital indemnity, dental care, vision care, disability income, long-
8 term care, student health insurance coverage, Medicare supplement insurance
9 coverage, or other limited benefit coverage; to short-term, limited-duration
10 health insurance coverage; or to benefit plans that are paid directly to an
11 individual insured or to the individual’s assigns and for which the amount of
12 the benefit is not based on potential medical costs or actual costs incurred.
13 Premium rates and rules for the classification of risk for Medicare supplement
14 insurance policies shall be governed by section 4051 of this title.
15 (2) The policy forms for major medical insurance coverage, as well as
16 the policy forms, premium rates, and rules for the classification of risk for the
17 other lines of insurance described in subdivision (1) of this subsection shall be
18 reviewed and approved or disapproved by the Commissioner. In making a
19 determination, the Commissioner shall consider whether a policy form,
20 premium rate, or rule is affordable and is not unjust, unfair, inequitable,
21 misleading, or contrary to the laws of this State; and, for a policy form for
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 23 of 181
1 major medical insurance coverage, whether it ensures equal access to
2 appropriate mental health care in a manner equivalent to other aspects of health
3 care as part of an integrated, holistic system of care. The Commissioner shall
4 make a determination within 30 days after the date the insurer filed the policy
5 form, premium rate, or rule with the Department. At the expiration of the 30-
6 day period, the form, premium rate, or rule shall be deemed approved unless
7 prior to then it has been affirmatively approved or disapproved by the
8 Commissioner or found to be incomplete. The Commissioner shall notify a
9 health insurer in writing if the insurer files any form, premium rate, or rule
10 containing a provision that does not meet the standards expressed in this
11 subsection. In such notice, the Commissioner shall state that a hearing will be
12 granted within 20 days upon the insurer’s written request.
13 (i) Notwithstanding the procedures and timelines set forth in subsections
14 (a) through (e) of this section, the Board may establish, by rule, a streamlined
15 rate review process for certain rate decisions, including proposed rates
16 affecting fewer than a minimum number of covered lives and proposed rates
17 for which a de minimis increase, as defined by the Board by rule, is sought.

3 § 4028. FORM AND CONTENTS OF POLICY
4 No policy of individual health insurance shall be delivered or issued for
5 delivery to any person in this State unless all of the following conditions are
6 met:
7 (1) The policy sets forth all of the monetary and other considerations for
8 the policy.
9 (2) The policy sets forth the time at which the insurance takes effect and
10 terminates.
11 (3) The policy purports to insure only one person, except that a policy
12 may insure, originally or by subsequent amendment, upon the application of an
13 adult member of a family who shall be deemed the policyholder, any two or
14 more eligible members of that family, including a spouse or civil union
15 partner, dependent children or any children under a specified age that shall not
16 exceed 26 years of age, and any other person dependent upon the policyholder.
17 (4) The style, arrangement, and overall appearance of the policy give no
18 undue prominence to any portion of the text, and every printed portion of the
19 text of the policy and of any endorsements or attached papers is plainly printed
20 in light-faced type of a style in general use, the size of which shall be uniform
21 and not less than 10-point with a lowercase unspaced alphabet length not less
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 25 of 181
1 than 120-point. As used in this subdivision, the “text” includes all printed
2 matter except the name and address of the insurer; the name or title of the
3 policy; the brief description, if any; and the captions and subcaptions.
4 (5) The exceptions and reductions of indemnity are set forth in the
5 policy and, except those that are set forth in sections 4029 and 4030 of this
6 title, are printed, at the insurer’s option, either with the benefit provision to
7 which they apply or under an appropriate caption such as “EXCEPTIONS” or
8 “EXCEPTIONS AND REDUCTIONS”; provided, however, that if an
9 exception or reduction specifically applies only to a particular benefit of the
10 policy, the statement of the exception or reduction shall be included with the
11 benefit provision to which it applies.
12 (6) Each policy form, including riders and endorsements, is identified by
13 a form number in the lower left-hand corner of the first page of the form.
14 (7) The policy does not contain any provision purporting to make any
15 portion of the charter, rules, constitution, or bylaws of the health insurer a part
16 of the policy unless that portion is set forth in full in the policy, except in the
17 case of the incorporation of, or reference to, a statement of rates or
18 classification of risks or a short-rate table filed with the Commissioner.
19 (8) Either prominently printed on or attached to the first page of the
20 policy is a notice to the effect that during a period of 30 days following the
21 date the policy is delivered to persons eligible for Medicare by reason of age,
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 26 of 181
1 and 10 days following the date of delivery to all other persons, the policy may
2 be surrendered to the insurer together with a written request for cancellation of
3 the policy, and that in such event, the insurer will refund any premium paid,
4 including any policy fees or other charges; provided, however, that this
5 subdivision shall not apply to single premium nonrenewable policies insuring
6 against accident only or medical costs or accidental bodily injury only.

11 § 4031. OMISSION OF INAPPLICABLE OR INCONSISTENT
12 STANDARD PROVISIONS

14 inapplicable to or inconsistent with the coverage provided by a particular form

17 modify any inconsistent provision or part of the provision in such manner as to
18 make the provision as contained in the policy consistent with the coverage
19 provided by the policy.

2 The provisions specified in sections 4029 and 4030 of this title, or any
3 corresponding provisions used in lieu of those provisions as permitted by those
4 sections, shall either be printed in the same order as the provisions are set forth
5 in those sections or, at the option of the health insurer, any such provision may
6 appear as a unit in any part of the policy, with other provisions to which it may
7 be logically related, provided the resulting policy shall not be in whole or in
8 part unintelligible, uncertain, ambiguous, abstruse, or likely to mislead a
9 person to whom the policy is offered, delivered, or issued.
10 § 4033. DISCRETIONARY CLAUSES PROHIBITED
11 (a) The purpose of this section is to ensure that health insurance benefits,
12 disability income protection coverage, and life insurance benefits are
13 contractually guaranteed and to avoid the conflict of interest that may occur
14 when the carrier responsible for providing benefits has discretionary authority
15 to decide what benefits are due. Nothing in this section shall be construed to
16 impose any requirement or duty on any person other than a health insurer or a
17 health insurer offering disability income protection coverage or life insurance.
18 (b) As used in this section:
19 (1) “Disability income protection coverage” means a policy, contract,
20 certificate, or agreement that provides for weekly, monthly, or other periodic
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 44 of 181
1 payments for a specified period during the continuance of disability resulting
2 from illness, injury, or a combination of illness and injury.
3 (2) “Health insurer” has the same meaning as in section 4021 of this
4 chapter and, as used in this section, also includes entities offering policies for
5 specific disease, accident, injury, hospital indemnity, dental care, disability
6 income, long-term care, and other limited benefit coverage.
7 (3) “Life insurance” means a policy, contract, certificate, or agreement
8 that provides life insurance as defined in subdivision 3301(a)(1) of this title.
9 (c) No policy, contract, certificate, or agreement offered or issued in this
10 State by a health insurer to provide, deliver, arrange for, pay for, or reimburse
11 any of the costs of health care services may contain a provision purporting to
12 reserve discretion to the health insurer to interpret the terms of the contract or
13 to provide standards of interpretation or review that are inconsistent with the
14 laws of this State, and any such provision in a policy, contract, certificate, or
15 agreement shall be null and void.
16 (d) No policy, contract, certificate, or agreement offered or issued in this
17 State providing for disability income protection coverage may contain a
18 provision purporting to reserve discretion to the insurer to interpret the terms
19 of the contract or to provide standards of interpretation or review that are
20 inconsistent with the laws of this State, and any such provision in a policy,
21 contract, certificate, or agreement shall be null and void.
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 45 of 181
1 (e) No policy, contract, certificate, or agreement of life insurance offered or
2 issued in this State shall contain a provision purporting to reserve discretion to
3 the insurer to interpret the terms of the contract or to provide standards of
4 interpretation or review that are inconsistent with the laws of this State, and
5 any such provision in a policy, contract, certificate, or agreement shall be null
6 and void.
7 § 4034. REQUIREMENTS OF OTHER JURISDICTIONS
8 (a) Any policy of a foreign or alien insurer, when delivered or issued for
9 delivery to any person in this State, may contain any provision that is not less
10 favorable to the covered individual than the provisions of this chapter and that
11 is prescribed or required by the law of the state under which the insurer is
12 organized.
13 (b) Any policy of a domestic health insurer, when issued for delivery in any
14 other state or country, may contain any provision permitted or required by the
15 laws of such other state or country.
16 § 4035. POLICIES NOT AFFECTED
17 Nothing in sections 4018–4020, 4023, 4028–4032, 4034, 4036, and 4037 of
18 this title shall apply to or affect:
19 (1) any policy of workers’ compensation insurance or any policy of
20 liability insurance, with or without supplementary coverage;
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 46 of 181
1 (2) any policy or contract of reinsurance;
2 (3) any blanket or group policy of insurance enumerated in sections
3 4041–4043 and 4052 of this title, except as otherwise provided in those
4 sections; or
5 (4) life insurance, endowment, or annuity contracts, or contracts
6 supplemental to those contracts, that contain only such provisions relating to
7 accident and sickness insurance as:
8 (A) provide additional benefits in case of death or dismemberment or
9 loss of sight by accident; or
10 (B) operate to safeguard the contracts against lapse or to give a
11 special surrender value or special benefit or an annuity in the event that the
12 insured or annuitant becomes totally and permanently disabled, as defined by
13 the contract or supplemental contract.
14 § 4036. NONCONFORMING POLICIES
15 (a) A health insurance policy shall not contain any provision that makes the
16 policy or any portion of the policy less favorable in any respect to the covered
17 individual than the provisions of the policy that are regulated by sections 4029
18 and 4030 of this title.
19 (b) A policy delivered or issued for delivery to any person in this State in
20 violation of sections 4029 and 4030 of this title shall be held valid but shall be
21 construed as provided in this chapter. When any provision in a policy
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 47 of 181
1 regulated by sections 4029 and 4030 is in conflict with any provision of those
2 sections, the rights, duties, and obligations of the health insurer and the
3 covered individual shall be governed by the provisions of those sections.
4 § 4037. APPLICATIONS FOR INSURANCE
5 (a)(1) A covered individual shall not be bound by any statement made in an
6 application for a policy unless a copy of the application is attached to or
7 endorsed on the policy as a part of the policy when issued.
8 (2) If a policy delivered or issued for delivery to any person in this State
9 is reinstated or renewed and the covered individual or assignee of the policy
10 makes a written request to the health insurer for a copy of the application, if
11 any, for such reinstatement or renewal, the health insurer shall deliver or mail a
12 copy of the application to the individual making the request within 15 days
13 after the receipt of the request. If the health insurer does not deliver or mail the
14 copy within 15 days, the health insurer shall be precluded from introducing the
15 application as evidence in any action or proceeding based on or involving the
16 policy or its reinstatement or renewal.
17 (b) No alteration of a written application for a policy shall be made by any
18 person other than the applicant without the applicant’s written consent, except
19 that insertions may be made by the health insurer, for administrative purposes
20 only, in a manner that indicates clearly that the insertions are not to be ascribed
21 to the applicant.
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 48 of 181
1 (c) The falsity of any statement in an application for a policy shall not bar
2 the right to recovery under the policy unless the false statement materially
3 affected either the acceptance of the risk or the hazard assumed by the health
4 insurer.
5 § 4038. RULEMAKING ON POLICY FILINGS
6 The Commissioner may adopt such reasonable rules concerning the
7 procedure for the filing or submission of policies subject to sections 4023 and
8 4028–4030 of this title as are necessary, proper, or advisable for the
9 administration of these sections. This provision shall not abridge any other
10 authority granted to the Commissioner by law.

4 § 4042. GROUP INSURANCE POLICIES; REQUIRED POLICY
5 PROVISIONS
6 (a) Terms and conditions. No group health insurance policy shall contain
7 any provision relating to notice of claim, proofs of loss, time of payment of
8 claims, or time within which legal action must be brought upon the policy that,
9 in the opinion of the Commissioner, is less favorable to the persons insured
10 than would be permitted by the provisions set forth in section 4029 of this title.
11 In addition, each such policy shall contain in substance the following
12 provisions:
13 (1) A provision that the policy; the application of the policyholder, if an
14 application or copy is attached to the policy; and the individual applications, if
15 any, submitted by the employees or members in connection with the policy
16 shall constitute the entire contract between the parties, and that all statements,
17 in the absence of fraud, made by any applicant or applicants shall be deemed
18 representations and not warranties, and that no such statement shall avoid the
19 insurance or reduce benefits under the policy unless contained in a written
20 application, of which a copy is attached to the policy.
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 54 of 181
1 (2) A provision that the health insurer will furnish to the policyholder,
2 for delivery to each employee or member of the insured group, an individual
3 certificate setting forth in summary form a statement of the essential features
4 of the insurance coverage of the employee or member and to whom benefits
5 are payable under the policy. If dependents are included in the coverage, only
6 one certificate need be issued for each family unit.
7 (3) A provision that to the group originally insured may be added from
8 time to time eligible new employees or members or dependents, as the case
9 may be, in accordance with the terms of the policy.
10 (4) A provision that the health insurer shall not exclude part-time
11 employees and shall offer the same group health benefits to part-time
12 employees as it offers to the employee groups of which the part-time
13 employees would be members if they were full-time employees. The health
14 insurer shall offer to include the part-time employees as part of the employer’s
15 employee group, at the full rate to be paid by the employer and the employee,
16 at a rate prorated between the employer and the employee, or at the employee’s
17 expense. As used in this subdivision, “part-time employee” means any
18 employee who works a minimum of at least 17.5 hours per week.
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30

1 (b) Protections for covered individuals.

13 Subchapter 4. Continuation and Conversion of
14 Group Health Insurance Policies
15 § 4047a. CONTINUATION OF GROUP
16 (a) All group major medical insurance and dental insurance policies shall
17 provide that any person whose insurance under the group policy would
18 terminate because of the occurrence of a qualifying event as defined in
19 subsection (b) of this section shall be entitled to continue the person’s health
20 insurance under that group policy.
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 59 of 181
1 (b) For purposes of this subchapter, “qualifying event” means:
2 (1) loss of employment, including a reduction in hours that results in
3 ineligibility for employer-sponsored coverage;
4 (2) divorce, dissolution, or legal separation of the covered employee
5 from the employee’s spouse or civil union partner;
6 (3) a dependent child ceasing to qualify as a dependent child under the
7 generally applicable requirements of the policy; or
8 (4) death of the covered employee or member.
9 (c) The provisions of this section shall not apply if one or more of the
10 following conditions applies:
11 (1) The deceased person or employee was not insured under the group
12 policy on the date of the qualifying event.
13 (2) The person is covered by Medicare.
14 (3) The person is covered by any other group insured or uninsured
15 arrangement that provides dental coverage or hospital and medical coverage
16 for individuals in a group and under which the person was not covered
17 immediately prior to the qualifying event, and no preexisting condition
18 exclusion applies; provided, however, that the person shall remain eligible for
19 continuation coverages that are not available under the insured or uninsured
20 arrangement.
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 60 of 181
1 (4) The person has a loss of employment due to misconduct as defined
2 in 21 V.S.A. § 1344.
3 (d) The continuation required by this section only applies to major medical
4 insurance and dental insurance benefits.
5 (e) Notice of the continuation privilege shall be included in each certificate
6 of coverage and shall be provided by the employer to the employee within 30
7 days following the occurrence of any qualifying event.
8 § 4047b. CONTINUATION; NOTICE; TERMS
9 (a) A person electing continuation shall notify the health insurer, or the
10 policyholder, or the contractor, or agent for the group if the policyholder did
11 not contract for the policy directly with the health insurer, of such election in
12 writing within 60 days after receiving notice following the occurrence of a
13 qualifying event pursuant to subsection 4047a(e) of this title. Notice of
14 election to continue under the group policy shall be accompanied by the initial
15 contribution, which shall include payment for the period from the qualifying
16 event through the end of the month in which the election is made.
17 (b) Contributions shall be due on a monthly basis in advance to the health
18 insurer or the health insurer’s agent, and shall not be more than 102 percent of
19 the group rate for the insurance being continued under the group policy on the
20 due date of each payment.
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 61 of 181
1 § 4047c. TERMINATION OF COVERAGE
2 Continuation of insurance under the group policy shall terminate upon the
3 occurrence of any of the following:
4 (1) The date 18 months after the date that insurance under the policy
5 would have terminated due to a qualifying event, as defined in subsection
6 4047a(b) of this title.
7 (2) The person fails to make timely payment of the required
8 contribution.
9 (3) The person is covered by Medicare.
10 (4) The person is covered by any other group insured or uninsured
11 arrangement that provides dental coverage or hospital and medical coverage
12 for individuals in a group, under which the person was not covered
13 immediately prior to the occurrence of a qualifying event, as defined in
14 subsection 4047a(b) of this title, and no preexisting condition exclusion
15 applies; provided, however, that the person shall remain eligible for
16 continuation coverages that are not available under the insured or uninsured
17 arrangement.
18 (5) The date on which the group policy is terminated or, in the case of
19 an employee, the date on which the decedent’s or terminated employee’s
20 employer terminates participation under the group policy. If such coverage is
21 replaced by similar coverage under another group policy:
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 62 of 181
1 (A) the person shall have the right to become covered under that
2 replacement policy for the balance of the period that the person would have

4 (B) the minimum level of benefits to be provided by the replacement
5 policy shall be the applicable level of benefits of the prior group policy
6 reduced by any benefits payable under that prior group policy; and
7 (C) the prior group policy shall continue to provide benefits to the

10 Subchapter 5. Group Health Insurance Termination and Replacement
11 § 4048a. DEFINITIONS; POLICIES AND CONTRACTS COVERED
12 (a) As used in this subchapter, “group health insurance policy or subscriber
13 contract” means a policy or contract that meets the following conditions:
14 (1) coverage is provided through insurance policies or subscriber
15 contracts to classes of employees or members of an organization or group;
16 (2) the coverage is not available to the general public and can be
17 obtained and maintained only because of the covered individual’s employment
18 or membership in an organization or group;
19 (3) there are arrangements for bulk payment of premiums or
20 subscription charges to the health insurer; and
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 63 of 181
1 (4) there is sponsorship of the plan by the employer, organization, or
2 group.
3 (b) A group health insurance policy or subscriber contract shall not be
4 issued or provided by a health insurer unless the policy or contract complies
5 with the provisions of this subchapter and the rules adopted pursuant to this
6 subchapter.
7 § 4048b. TERMINATION FOR NONPAYMENT OF PREMIUM OR
8 SUBSCRIPTION CHARGES
9 (a) If a group health insurance policy or subscriber contract provides for
10 automatic termination of the policy or contract after a premium or subscription
11 charge has remained unpaid through the grace period allowed for such
12 payment, the health insurer shall be liable for valid claims for covered losses
13 incurred prior to the end of the grace period.
14 (b) If the actions of the health insurer after the end of the grace period
15 indicate that it considers the policy or contract to be continuing in force beyond
16 the end of the grace period, including actions such as continuing to recognize
17 claims subsequently incurred, the health insurer shall be liable for valid claims
18 for losses incurred prior to the effective date of written notice of termination to
19 the policyholder or other entity responsible for making payments or submitting
20 subscription charges to the health insurer.
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 64 of 181
1 (c) The health insurer shall notify a policyholder or other responsible entity
2 of any premium payment due on a policy at least 21 days before the due date.
3 The effective date of termination of a policy or contract shall not be prior to
4 midnight at the end of the 14th day following mailing of notice of termination.
5 § 4048c. NOTICE OF TERMINATION
6 (a) A notice of termination of a health insurer’s group health insurance
7 policy or subscriber contract shall:
8 (1) request the group policyholder or other entity involved to notify
9 employees or members covered under the policy or subscriber contract of the
10 date of termination of the policy or contract and to advise the employees or
11 members that, unless otherwise provided in the policy or contract, the health
12 insurer shall not be liable for claims for losses incurred after such date; and
13 (2) advise, in any instance in which the plan involves employee
14 contributions, that if the policyholder or other entity continues to collect
15 contributions for the coverage beyond the date of termination, the policyholder
16 or other entity may be held solely liable for the benefits with respect to which
17 the contributions have been collected.
18 (b) The health insurer giving notice of termination shall prepare and furnish
19 to the policyholder or other entity at the time of notice a supply of a notice
20 form to be distributed to covered employees or members. The form shall state
21 the fact of termination and the effective date of termination. The form shall
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 65 of 181
1 contain a statement directing employees or members to refer to their
2 certificates or contracts in order to determine their rights.
3 § 4048d. EXTENSION OF BENEFITS
4 (a) Each group health insurance policy or subscriber contract shall provide
5 a reasonable extension of benefits in the event that the employer or member is
6 in a condition of total disability on the date of termination of the group policy
7 or contract in accordance with the provisions of this section.
8 (b) A policy or contract providing benefits for loss of time from work or
9 specific indemnity during hospital confinement shall provide that termination
10 of the policy or contract during a loss of time or confinement shall have no
11 effect on benefits payable for the loss of time or confinement.
12 (c) A policy or contract providing hospital or medical expense coverage
13 benefits shall provide an extension of benefits of at least 12 months under
14 major medical insurance coverage and at least 90 days under other types of
15 hospital or medical expense coverage.
16 (d) The provisions of a policy or contract relating to extension of benefits
17 or accrued liability shall be described in the policy or contract as well as in
18 group insurance certificates. The benefits payable during a period of extension
19 or accrued liability may be subject to the policy’s or contract’s regular benefit
20 limits.

1 (e) Nothing in this section shall be construed to require an extension of

3 § 4048e. REPLACEMENT COVERAGE
4 (a) General. When the group health insurance policy or subscriber contract
5 of a health insurer replaces a policy or contract providing similar benefits of
6 another health insurer, the liability of both health insurers shall be as provided
7 in this section and rules adopted pursuant to this section.
8 (b) Liability of prior health insurer. A prior health insurer remains liable
9 after termination of its policy or contract only to the extent of its accrued
10 liabilities and extensions of benefits.
11 (c) Liability of succeeding health insurer.
12 (1) A succeeding health insurer shall offer a group health insurance
13 policy or subscriber contract to replace a prior health insurer’s policy or
14 contract in accordance with the provisions of this subsection.
15 (2) A succeeding health insurer shall offer a policy or contract to cover
16 all persons who:
17 (A) are covered or are a member of a class eligible for coverage
18 under the prior health insurer’s policy or contract on the date of termination of
19 the prior health insurer’s policy or contract; or
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 67 of 181
1 (B) are a member of a class eligible for coverage under the
2 succeeding health insurer’s policy or contract on the date of termination of the
3 prior health insurer’s policy or contract.
4 (3) The succeeding health insurer is not liable under this subsection for
5 benefits required to be paid by the prior health insurer.
6 (4) When replacing a prior health insurer’s plan that is not subject to
7 section 4048d of this title, the succeeding health insurer shall, in addition to the
8 coverage required to be offered under subdivision (2) of this subsection, offer a
9 policy or contract that provides a level of benefit equal to the lesser of:
10 (A) the extension of benefits that would have been required if the
11 prior health insurer’s policy or contract was subject to section 4048d of this
12 title; or
13 (B) the extension of benefits required for the succeeding health
14 insurer’s policy or contract, except that any such benefits may be reduced by
15 benefits actually payable under the prior health insurer’s plan.
16 (5) The preexisting condition limitation of a succeeding health insurer’s
17 policy or contract shall provide a level of benefits equal to the lesser of:
18 (A) the benefits of the succeeding health insurer’s policy or contract
19 determined without application of the preexisting conditions limitation; or
20 (B) the benefits of the prior health insurer’s policy or contract.
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 68 of 181
1 (6) The succeeding health insurer, in applying a deductible or waiting-
2 period provision in its policy or contract, shall give credit for the satisfaction of
3 the same or similar provisions under the prior health insurer’s policy or
4 contract.
5 (7) At the succeeding health insurer’s request, the prior health insurer
6 shall furnish all information needed to determine the benefits available under
7 the prior health insurer’s policy or contract.
8 (d) Rules. The Commissioner shall adopt rules necessary to carry out the
9 purposes of this section.
10 Subchapter 6. Other Forms of Health Coverage
11 § 4051. MEDICARE SUPPLEMENT INSURANCE POLICIES
12 (a) Community rating.
13 (1) A health insurer shall use a community rating method acceptable to
14 the Commissioner for determining premiums for Medicare supplement
15 insurance policies.
16 (2) The Commissioner shall adopt rules for standards and procedure for
17 permitting health insurers that issue Medicare supplement insurance policies to
18 use one or more risk classifications in their community rating method. The
19 premium charged shall not deviate from the community rate and the rules shall
20 not permit medical underwriting and screening, except that a health insurer
21 may set different community rates for persons eligible for Medicare by reason
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 69 of 181
1 of age and persons eligible for Medicare by reason of disability.
2 (b) Premium increases.
3 (1) Within five days after receiving a request for approval of any
4 composite average rate increase in excess of three percent, or any other
5 coverage changes that the Commissioner determines will have a comparable
6 impact on cost or availability of coverage for a Medicare supplement insurance
7 policy issued by any health insurer with 5,000 or more total lives in the
8 Vermont Medicare supplement insurance market, the Commissioner shall
9 notify the Department of Disabilities, Aging, and Independent Living of the
10 proposed premium increase. A composite average rate is the enrollment-
11 weighted average rate increase of all plans offered by a health insurer.
12 (2) Within five days after receiving notification pursuant to subdivision
13 (1) of this subsection, the Department of Disabilities, Aging, and Independent
14 Living shall inform the members of the Advisory Board established pursuant to
15 33 V.S.A. § 505 of the proposed premium increase.
16 (3)(A) The Commissioner shall not approve any request to increase
17 Medicare supplement insurance premium rates unless the amount of the rate
18 increase complies with the statutory standards for approval under sections
19 4026, 4513, 4584, and 5104 of this title. Any approved rate increase shall not
20 be based on an unreasonable change in loss ratio from the previous year, unless
21 the Commissioner makes written findings that such change is necessary to
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 70 of 181
1 prevent a substantial adverse impact on the financial condition of the health
2 insurer. In acting on such rate increase requests, the Commissioner may deny
3 the request, approve the rate increase as requested, or approve a rate increase in
4 an amount different from the increase requested. A decision by the
5 Commissioner other than an approval of the rate requested may be appealed by
6 the health insurer, provided that the burden of proof shall be on the health
7 insurer to show that the approved rate does not meet the statutory standards
8 established under this subsection.
9 (B) Before acting on the rate increase requested, the Commissioner
10 may make such examination or investigation as the Commissioner deems
11 necessary, including where applicable the review process set forth in
12 subdivision (C) of this subdivision (3).
13 (C)(i) In reviewing any Medicare supplement insurance rate increase
14 for which an independent analysis has been performed pursuant to 33 V.S.A.
15 § 6706 and in which the health insurer’s requested composite average increase,
16 the independent expert’s recommended composite average rate increase, or the
17 Department actuary’s recommended composite average rate increase differ by
18 two percentage points or more, the Commissioner shall hold a public hearing at
19 which the health insurer, the Department’s actuary, the independent expert, any
20 intervenor, and the public will have the opportunity to present written and oral
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 71 of 181
1 testimony and will be available to answer questions of the Commissioner and
2 those present.
3 (ii) The hearing shall be noticed and held at a time and place so as
4 to facilitate public participation, and shall be recorded and become part of the
5 record before the Commissioner. At the Commissioner’s discretion, the
6 hearing may be conducted remotely.
7 (iii) If the carrier’s requested composite average increase, the
8 independent expert’s recommended composite average increase, or the
9 Department actuary’s recommended composite average increase differs by less
10 than two percentage points, the Department and the parties shall confer by
11 conference call, or by any other available media, to review the rate requests
12 and recommendations. However, a public hearing may be held at the

8 (c) Disability.
9 (1) A health insurer that issues Medicare supplement insurance policies

6 § 4052. BLANKET HEALTH INSURANCE
7 (a) Blanket health insurance is a form of health insurance that, to the extent
8 permitted under federal law, is supplemental to major medical health insurance
9 or provides coverage other than the payment of all or a portion of the cost of
10 health care services or products, and that covers special groups of persons as
11 follows:
12 (1) under a policy or contract issued to any common carrier, which shall
13 be deemed the policyholder, covering a group defined as all persons who may
14 become passengers on such common carrier;
15 (2) under a policy or contract issued to an employer, who shall be
16 deemed the policyholder, covering any group of employees defined by
17 reference to exceptional hazards incident to such employment;
18 (3) under a policy or contract issued to a public school, independent
19 school, or approved education program, as those terms are defined in
20 16 V.S.A. § 11; to a postsecondary school, as defined in 16 V.S.A.
21 § 176(b)(1); or to a prequalified private prekindergarten provider, as defined in
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 74 of 181
1 16 V.S.A. § 829(a)(3), or to the head or principal of the school, program, or
2 provider, who or which shall be deemed the policyholder, covering students or
3 teachers, or both;
4 (4) under a policy or contract issued in the name of any volunteer fire
5 department, emergency medical services provider, or other such volunteer
6 group, which shall be deemed the policyholder, covering all of the members of
7 the department or group in connection with their department or group
8 activities; or
9 (5) under a policy or contract issued to any other substantially similar
10 group that, in the discretion of the Commissioner and after the prior approval
11 by the Commissioner of the group, may be subject to the issuance of a blanket
12 health policy or contract.
13 (b)(1) No blanket health insurance policy shall contain any provision
14 relating to notice of claim, proofs of loss, time of payment of claims, or time
15 within which legal action must be brought upon the policy that, in the opinion
16 of the Commissioner, is less favorable to the persons insured than would be
17 permitted by the provisions set forth in section 4029 of this title.
18 (2) An individual application shall not be required from a person
19 covered under a blanket health policy or contract, nor shall it be necessary for
20 the insurer to furnish each person a certificate.
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 75 of 181
1 (3) All benefits under any blanket health policy shall, unless for hospital
2 and physician service or surgical benefits, be payable to the person insured, or
3 to the person’s designated beneficiary or beneficiaries, or to the person’s
4 estate, except that if the person insured is a minor, the benefits may be made
5 payable to the minor’s parent, guardian, or other person actually supporting the
6 minor.
7 (4) Nothing in this section shall be deemed to affect the legal liability of
8 policyholders for the death of, or injury to, any members of the group.
9 (c) No blanket health insurance policy that provides coverage for the
10 payment of all or a portion of the cost of health care services or products shall
11 contain any provision that does not comply with a requirement of this title, or a
12 rule adopted pursuant to this title applicable to health insurance, other than
13 those requirements applicable to nongroup health insurance or small group
14 health insurance. The Commissioner may waive the application to a blanket
15 insurance policy of one or more of the health insurance requirements of this
16 title, or a rule adopted pursuant to this title, if the requirement is not relevant to
17 the types of risks and duration of risks insured against in the blanket insurance
18 policy.
19 § 4053. SHORT-TERM, LIMITED-DURATION HEALTH INSURANCE

18 consumer protections that are and are not included. The Commissioner shall
19 determine the specific disclosure language that shall be used in all short-term,
20 limited-duration health insurance policies, contracts, and application materials

1 § 4057. COVERAGE OF CHILDREN
2 (a) Definition. “Health insurance plan” has the same meaning as in section
3 4011 of this chapter and shall be subject to the same excepted benefits, in each
4 case, as set forth in 45 C.F.R. § 146.145, as in effect as of December 31, 2017.
5 (b) Newborn coverage.
6 (1) A health insurance plan that provides dependent coverage of
7 children shall also provide that health insurance benefits applicable to children
8 are payable with respect to a newly born child of the insured or subscriber
9 from the moment of birth. Coverage for a newly born child shall include
10 coverage of injury, sickness, and necessary care and treatment of medically
11 diagnosed congenital defect or birth abnormality.
12 (2) Coverage for a newly born child shall be provided without notice or
13 additional premium for not less than 60 days after the date of birth. If payment
14 of a specific premium or subscription fee is required in order to have the
15 coverage continue beyond such 60-day period, the policy may require that
16 notification of the birth of the newly born child and payment of the required
17 premium or fees be furnished to the health insurer within a period of not less
18 than 60 days after the date of birth.
19 (c) Adopted child coverage.
20 (1) As used in this section:
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 79 of 181
1 (A) “Child” means, in connection with any adoption or placement for
2 adoption of the child, an individual who has not attained 18 years of age as of
3 the date of the adoption or placement for adoption.
4 (B) “Placement for adoption” means the assumption and retention by
5 a person of a legal obligation for total or partial support of a child in
6 anticipation of the adoption of the child. The child’s placement with a person
7 terminates upon the termination of such legal obligations.
8 (2) In any case in which a health insurance plan provides coverage for
9 dependent children of covered individuals, the plan shall provide benefits to
10 dependent children placed with covered individuals for adoption under the
11 same terms and conditions as apply to the natural, dependent children of the
12 covered individuals, irrespective of whether the adoption has become final.
13 (3) A health insurance plan shall not restrict coverage under the plan of
14 any dependent child adopted by a covered individual, or placed with a covered
15 individual for adoption, solely on the basis of a preexisting condition of the
16 child at the time that the child would otherwise become eligible for coverage
17 under the plan, if the adoption or placement for adoption occurs while the
18 covered individual is eligible for coverage under the plan.
19 (d) Coverage required until 26 years of age. A health insurance plan that
20 provides dependent coverage of children shall continue to make that coverage
21 available for an adult child until the child attains 26 years of age, provided that
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 80 of 181
1 this subsection shall not apply to a plan providing coverage for a specified
2 disease or other limited benefit coverage, and further provided that nothing in
3 this subsection shall require a plan to make coverage available for the child of
4 a child receiving dependent coverage.
5 (e) Coverage of adult child with a disability.
6 (1) A health insurance plan that provides for terminating the coverage of
7 a dependent child upon attainment of the limiting age for dependent children
8 specified in the policy shall not limit or restrict coverage with respect to an
9 unmarried child who meets all of the following criteria:

12 would qualify the child for benefits using the definitions, standards, and
13 methodology in 20 C.F.R. Part 404, Subpart P;
14 (B) became so incapable prior to attainment of the limiting age; and
15 (C) is chiefly dependent upon the employee, member, subscriber, or
16 policyholder for support and maintenance.
17 (2) Coverage under subdivision (1) of this subsection shall not be denied
18 any person based upon the existence of such a condition; provided, however,
19 that a health insurance plan may require reasonable periodic proof of a
20 continuing condition not more frequently than once every year.

10 § 4058. MEDICAL SUPPORT ORDERS
11 (a) As used in this section:
12 (1) “Dependent coverage” means family coverage, or coverage for one
13 or more persons as long as the coverage for one or more persons is greater than
14 or equal to the coverage available under family coverage.
15 (2) “Health insurance plan” has the same meaning as in section 4011 of
16 this chapter and shall be subject to the same excepted benefits, in each case, as
17 set forth in 45 C.F.R. § 146.145, as in effect as of December 31, 2017.
18 (b) A health insurer shall not deny enrollment of a child under the health
19 insurance plan of the child’s parent who is ordered to provide medical support
20 on the grounds that:
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 83 of 181
1 (1) the child was born to unmarried parents;
2 (2) the child is not claimed as a dependent on the parent’s federal tax
3 return; or
4 (3) the child does not reside with the parent or in the health insurer’s
5 service area.
6 (c) When a parent is required by a court or administrative order to provide
7 health coverage for a child, and the parent is eligible for dependent health
8 coverage, the health insurer shall be required:
9 (1) To enroll, under the dependent coverage, a child who is otherwise
10 eligible for the coverage without regard to any enrollment season restrictions
11 or any seasonal restrictions on switching from one plan to another, upon
12 application of either parent, the employer, the State agency administering the
13 Medicaid program, any State agency administering health benefits or a health
14 insurance plan for which Medicaid is a source of funding, or the child support
15 enforcement program.
16 (2) Not to disenroll or eliminate coverage of the child unless the health
17 insurer is provided satisfactory written evidence that:
18 (A) the court or administrative order is no longer in effect;
19 (B) the child is or will be enrolled in comparable health coverage
20 through another health insurer that will take effect not later than the effective
21 date of disenrollment; or
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 84 of 181
1 (C) the employer has eliminated dependent health coverage for all of
2 its employees if allowed by law.
3 (3) To provide enrollment under subdivision (1) of this subsection with
4 coverage effective three days after the mailing of notice of the court or
5 administrative order to the health insurer or upon actual receipt of notice by the
6 health insurer, whichever is sooner. The health insurer shall have 10 days from
7 notice to process the enrollment and shall be entitled to premiums from the
8 effective date of enrollment.
9 (d) A health insurer shall not impose requirements on a State agency that
10 has been assigned the rights of an individual eligible for medical assistance
11 under Medicaid and covered for health benefits from the health insurer that are
12 different from requirements applicable to an agent or assignee of any other
13 individual so covered.
14 (e) Any health insurer that fails to enroll a child after notice under
15 15 V.S.A. § 663(d) or 33 V.S.A. § 4110(a)(4) shall be directly liable for any
16 medical expenses of the child that would have been covered under the health
17 insurance plan had the health insurer enrolled the child upon receiving notice.
18 (f) Notice by first class mail, postage prepaid, or by any other method
19 showing actual receipt, shall be presumptive evidence of its receipt by the
20 health insurer to whom it is addressed. Any period of time that is determined
21 under this section by the giving of notice shall commence to run from the date
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 85 of 181
1 of mailing, if the notice is mailed, or the date of actual receipt if another
2 method of transmitting the notice is used.
3 (g) A health insurer may cancel any health insurance plan that is the subject
4 of a medical support order for nonpayment of premium only if the health
5 insurer mails or delivers notice of cancellation to both parents and all other
6 persons or agencies identified in the medical support order. Any health insurer

10 § 4059. COVERAGE FOR CIVIL UNIONS

21 union.
