11 Subchapter 8. Internal and External Reviews
12 § 4063. INDEPENDENT EXTERNAL REVIEW OF HEALTH CARE
13 SERVICE DECISIONS
14 (a) As used in this section, “covered individual” includes a member of a
15 health insurance plan not otherwise subject to the Department’s jurisdiction
16 that has voluntarily agreed to use the external review process provided under
17 this section.
18 (b) A covered individual who has exhausted all applicable internal review
19 procedures provided by the health insurance plan shall have the right to an
20 independent external review of a decision under a health insurance plan to
21 deny, reduce, or terminate health care coverage or to deny payment for a health
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 87 of 181
1 care service. The independent review shall be available when requested in
2 writing by the affected covered individual, provided the decision to be
3 reviewed requires the plan to expend at least $100.00 for the service and the
4 decision by the plan is based on one of the following reasons:
5 (1) The health care service is a covered benefit that the health insurer
6 has determined to be not medically necessary.
7 (2) A limitation is placed on the selection of a health care provider that
8 is claimed by the covered individual to be inconsistent with limits imposed by
9 the health insurance plan and any applicable laws and rules.
10 (3) The health care treatment has been determined to be experimental or
11 investigational or is an off-label drug. A health insurance plan that denies use
12 of a prescription drug for the treatment of cancer as not medically necessary or
13 as an experimental or investigational use shall treat any internal appeal of such
14 denial as an emergency or urgent appeal and shall decide the appeal within the
15 time frames applicable to emergency and urgent internal appeals under rules
16 adopted by the Commissioner.
17 (4) The health care service involves a medically based decision that a
18 condition is preexisting.
19 (5) The decision involves an adverse determination related to surprise
20 medical billing, as established under Section 2799A-1 or 2799A-2 of the
21 Public Health Service Act, including with respect to whether an item or service
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 88 of 181
1 that is the subject of the adverse determination is an item or service to which
2 Section 2799A-1 or 2799A-2 of the Public Health Service Act, or both,
3 applies.
4 (c) The right to review under this section shall not be construed to change
5 the terms of coverage under a health insurance plan.
6 (d) The Department shall adopt rules necessary to carry out the purposes of
7 this section. The rules shall ensure that the independent external reviews have
8 the following characteristics:
9 (1) The independent external reviews shall be conducted:
10 (A) by independent review organizations pursuant to a contract with
11 the Department, and the reviewers shall include health care providers
12 credentialed with respect to the health care service under review and shall have
13 no conflict of interest relating to the performance of their duties under this
14 section; and
15 (B) in accordance with standards of decision making based on
16 objective clinical evidence, shall resolve all issues in a timely manner, and
17 shall provide expedited resolution when the decision relates to emergency or
18 urgent health care services.
19 (2) A covered individual shall:
20 (A) Be provided with adequate notice of the covered individual’s
21 review rights under this section.
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 89 of 181
1 (B) Have the right to use outside assistance during the review process
2 and to submit evidence relating to the health care service.
3 (C) Pay an application fee of $25.00 for each request for an
4 independent external review of an appealable decision not to exceed a total of
5 $75.00 annually. The application fee may be waived or reduced based on a
6 determination by the Commissioner that the financial circumstances of the
7 covered individual warrant a waiver or reduction. The application fee shall be
8 paid by the health insurer, not the covered individual, if the independent
9 review organization reverses the health insurer’s decision to deny payment for
10 a health care service.
11 (D) Be protected from retaliation for exercising the covered
12 individual’s right to an independent external review under this section.
13 (3) Other costs of the independent review shall be paid by the health
14 insurance plan.
15 (4) The independent review organization shall issue to both parties a
16 written review decision that is evidence-based. The decision shall be binding
17 on the health insurance plan.
18 (5) The confidentiality of any health care information acquired or
19 provided to the independent review organization shall be maintained in
20 compliance with any applicable State or federal laws.
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 90 of 181
1 (6) The records of, and internal materials prepared for, specific reviews
2 by any independent review organization under this section shall be exempt
3 from public inspection and copying under the Public Records Act.
4 (e) Decisions relating to the following health care services shall not be
5 reviewed under this section but shall be reviewed by the review process
6 provided by law:
7 (1) health care services provided by the Vermont Medicaid program or
8 Medicaid benefits provided through a contracted health plan; and
9 (2) health care services provided to incarcerated individuals by the
10 Department of Corrections.
11 § 4064. MENTAL HEALTH SERVICES REVIEW
12 (a) The purposes of this section are to:
13 (1) promote the delivery of quality mental health services in a cost-
14 effective manner;
15 (2) foster the practice of mental health services review as a professional
16 collaborative process, the primary objective of which is to enhance the
17 effectiveness of clinical treatment;
18 (3) protect clients and patients, employers, and mental health providers
19 by ensuring that review agents are qualified to perform service review
20 activities and to make informed decisions on the appropriateness of mental
21 health care; and
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 91 of 181
1 (4) ensure the confidentiality of clients’ and patients’ mental health
2 records in the performance of service review activities in accordance with
3 applicable State and federal laws.
4 (b) Definitions. As used in this section:
5 (1) “License” means a review agent’s license granted by the
6 Commissioner.
7 (2) “Mental health provider” means any individual, corporation, facility,
8 or institution certified or licensed by this State to provide mental health
9 services, including a physician, nurse with recognized psychiatric specialties,
10 hospital or other health care facility, psychologist, clinical social worker,
11 mental health counselor, alcohol or drug abuse counselor, or an employee or
12 agent of such mental health provider acting in the course and scope of
13 employment or an agency related to mental health services.
14 (3) “Mental health services” mean acts of diagnosis, treatment,
15 evaluation, or advice or any other acts permissible under the health care laws
16 of Vermont, whether performed in an outpatient or institutional setting, and
17 include treatment for substance use disorder.
18 (4) “Review agent” means a person or entity performing service review
19 activities within one year following the date of submission of a fully compliant
20 application for licensure who is affiliated with, under contract with, or acting
21 on behalf of a business entity in this State and who provides or administers
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 92 of 181
1 mental health benefits to members of health insurance plans subject to the
2 Department’s jurisdiction, including a health insurer.
3 (5) “Service review” means any system for reviewing the appropriate
4 and efficient allocation of mental health services given or proposed to be given
5 to a client or patient, or to a group of clients or patients, for the purpose of
6 recommending or determining whether the services should be covered and
7 includes activities of utilization review and managed care, but does not include
8 professional peer review that does not affect reimbursement for or provision of
9 services.
10 (c) Any person who approves or denies payment, or who recommends
11 approval or denial of payment, for mental health services, or whose review
12 results in approval or denial of payment for mental health services on a case-
13 by-case basis, shall not review these services in this State unless the
14 Commissioner has granted the person a review agent’s license. The
15 Commissioner shall adopt rules to implement the provisions of this section,
16 including the procedures and standards for licensure. The rules shall
17 differentiate between health maintenance organizations licensed to do business
18 within this State and other forms of utilization review. The rules shall
19 establish:
20 (1) A requirement that within 10 business days after receiving a request
21 for them, the review agent shall make available at no cost to the clients,
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 93 of 181
1 patients, and providers affected by its service review activities the specific
2 review criteria and standards, credentials of the reviewing professionals, and
3 procedures and methods to be used in evaluating proposed or delivered mental
4 health services.
5 (2) A time period within which any determination regarding the
6 provision or reimbursement of mental health services shall be made.
7 (3) A requirement that any determination regarding mental health
8 services rendered or to be rendered to a client or patient that may result in a
9 denial of third-party reimbursement or a denial of precertification for that
10 service shall include the evaluation, findings, and concurrence of a mental
11 health professional whose training and expertise is at least comparable to that
12 of the treating mental health provider.
13 (4) The type, qualifications, and number of personnel required to
14 perform service review activities.
15 (5) A requirement that a determination by a review agent that care
16 rendered or to be rendered is inappropriate shall not be made until the review
17 agent has communicated with the patient’s attending mental health provider
18 concerning that care. The review shall be prospective or concurrent with the
19 treatment.
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 94 of 181
1 (6) A requirement that any determination that care rendered or to be

6 organization pursuant to section 4063 of this title of an adverse decision by a

10 (8) Policies and procedures to ensure that all applicable State and federal

13 (9) Policies and procedures that ensure appropriate notification and

16 (10)(A) Prohibition of an agreement between the review agent and a

2025 Page 95 of 181

3 Subchapter 9. Required Covered Benefits
4 § 4067. APPLICATION OF SUBCHAPTER
5 (a) Unless otherwise specified and to the extent not inconsistent with
6 federal law, the benefits required in this subchapter:
7 (1) apply only to major medical insurance plans;
8 (2) may be subject to deductibles, co-payment and coinsurance amounts,
9 fee or benefit limits, practice parameters, and utilization review consistent with
10 any applicable rules and guidance adopted by the Department of Financial
11 Regulation; and
12 (3) do not apply to Vermont Medicaid.
13 (b) A health insurer may require benefits mandated in this subchapter to be
14 provided by a licensed health care provider under contract with the health
15 insurer; provided, however, that this provision shall not be construed to relieve
16 a health insurance plan from complying with the applicable network adequacy
17 requirements adopted by the Commissioner by rule.
18 § 4068. CHIROPRACTIC SERVICES
19 (a) A health insurance plan shall provide coverage for clinically necessary
20 health care services provided by a chiropractic physician licensed in this State
21 for treatment within the scope of practice described in 26 V.S.A. chapter 10,
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 97 of 181
1 but limiting adjunctive therapies to physiotherapy modalities and rehabilitative
2 exercises. A health insurance plan does not have to provide coverage for the
3 treatment of any visceral condition arising from problems or dysfunctions of
4 the abdominal or thoracic organs.
5 (b) A health insurer may require that the chiropractic services be
6 provided upon referral from a health care provider under contract with the
7 health insurer.
8 (c) For silver- and bronze-level qualified health benefit plans and any
9 reflective health benefit plans offered at the silver or bronze level pursuant to
10 33 V.S.A. chapter 18, subchapter 1, health care services provided by a
11 chiropractic physician may be subject to a co-payment requirement, provided
12 that any required co-payment amount shall be between 125 and 150 percent of
13 the amount of the co-payment applicable to care and services provided by a
14 primary care provider under the plan.
15 (d) Nothing in this section shall be construed as impeding or preventing
16 either the provision or coverage of health care services by licensed chiropractic
17 physicians, within the lawful scope of chiropractic practice, in hospital
18 facilities on a staff or employee basis.
19 § 4069. PROSTHETIC DEVICES
20 (a) As used in this section, “prosthetic device” means an artificial limb
21 device to replace, in whole or in part, an arm or a leg.
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 98 of 181
1 (b) A health insurance plan shall provide coverage for prosthetic devices
2 that is at least equivalent to the coverage provided by the federal Medicare
3 program. Coverage may be limited to the prosthetic device that is the most
4 appropriate model that is medically necessary to meet the patient’s medical
5 needs. Any dispute between the covered individual and the carrier concerning
6 coverage and the application of this section shall be subject to independent
7 external review under section 4063 of this title.
8 (c) A health insurance plan may require prior authorization for prosthetic
9 devices in the same manner and to the same extent as prior authorization is
10 required for any other covered benefit.
11 (d) A health insurance plan shall provide coverage under this section for
12 the medically necessary repair or replacement of a prosthetic device.
13 (e) The coverage for prosthetic devices shall not be subject to a deductible,
14 co-payment, or coinsurance provision that is less favorable to a covered
15 individual than the deductible, co-payment, or coinsurance provisions that
16 apply generally to other nonprimary care items and services under the health
17 insurance plan.

2025 Page 99 of 181
1 (a) As used in this section:
2 (1) “Hearing aid” means any small, wearable electronic instrument or

4 compensating for impaired human hearing and any related parts, attachments,
5 or accessories, including earmolds and associated remote microphones that

16 (C) programming of a hearing aid;
17 (D) hearing aid repairs;

20 (F) ear mold impressions; and
21 (G) auditory rehabilitation and training.

4 chapter 31, or an advanced practice registered nurse licensed under 26 V.S.A.
5 chapter 28, working within that professional’s scope of practice.

14 (b)(1) A large group health insurance plan shall cover the cost of a hearing

VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 101 of 181
1 expiration of the three-year period based on a hearing care professional’s

4 (c)(1) Subject to the limitations set forth in subdivision (b)(2) of this
5 section, the coverage provided by a large group health insurance plan for
6 hearing aids and associated services shall be limited only by medical necessity.
7 (2) A covered individual may select a hearing aid that exceeds the limits
8 set forth in subdivision (1) of this subsection and pay the additional cost.
9 (d) The coverage required by this section shall not be subject to a
10 deductible, co-payment, or coinsurance provision that is less favorable to a
11 covered individual than the deductible, co-payment, or coinsurance provisions
12 that apply generally to other nonprimary care items and services under the

18 health care services that:

VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 102 of 181
1 (B) are included in the State’s essential health benefits benchmark
2 plan.

6 (c) Cost sharing. A health insurance plan shall not impose greater
7 coinsurance, co-payment, deductible, or other cost-sharing requirements for
8 coverage of gender-affirming health care services than apply to the diagnosis

16 § 4072. MENTAL HEALTH AND SUBSTANCE USE DISORDER

18 (a) It is the goal of the General Assembly that treatment for mental

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 103 of 181

7 Classification of Diseases, as periodically revised.

14 agency related to mental health services.

16 limits, deductibles, copayments, coinsurance, and any other cost-sharing

18 component of health insurance coverage that affects the covered individual.

15 § 4073. DIABETES TREATMENT
16 (a) A health insurance plan shall provide coverage for the equipment,

18 medical nutrition therapy, for the treatment of insulin-dependent diabetes,

6 management of diabetes.
7 § 4074. TREATMENT OF INHERITED METABOLIC DISORDERS
8 (a) As used in this section:
9 (1) “Inherited metabolic disorder” means a disorder caused by an
10 inherited abnormality of body chemistry for which the State screens newborn
11 infants.
12 (2) “Low protein modified food product” means a food product that is
13 specifically formulated to have less than one gram of protein per serving and is
14 intended to be used under the direction of a health care professional for the
15 dietary treatment of a metabolic disorder.
16 (3) “Medical food” means an amino acid modified preparation that is
17 intended to be used under the direction of a health care professional for the
18 dietary treatment of an inherited metabolic disorder.
19 (b) A health insurance plan shall provide coverage for medical foods
20 prescribed for medically necessary treatment for an inherited metabolic
21 disorder.
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 112 of 181
1 (c) Coverage for low protein modified food products prescribed for
2 medically necessary treatment of an inherited metabolic disorder shall be at
3 least $2,500.00 during any continuous period of 12 months for any covered
4 individual.
5 § 4075. CRANIOFACIAL DISORDERS
6 (a)(1) A health insurance plan shall provide coverage for diagnosis and
7 medically necessary treatment, including surgical and nonsurgical procedures,
8 for a musculoskeletal disorder that affects any bone or joint in the face, neck,
9 or head and is the result of accident, trauma, congenital defect, developmental
10 defect, or pathology. Subject to subsection (b) of this section, this coverage
11 shall be the same as that provided under the health insurance plan for any other
12 musculoskeletal disorder in the body and shall be covered when the diagnosis
13 or treatment, or both, is prescribed or administered by a physician or a dentist.
14 (2) This section shall not be construed to require coverage for dental
15 services for the diagnosis or treatment of dental disorders or dental pathology
16 primarily affecting the gums, teeth, or alveolar ridge.
17 (b) A health insurance plan may require a referral from a health care
18 provider under contract with the plan.

1 § 4076. HOME HEALTH SERVICES
2 (a) As used in this section:
3 (1) “ Home health agency” means a nonprofit home health agency that
4 has been certified under Title XVIII of the Social Security Act (42 U.S.C.
5 § 1395 et seq.).
6 (2) “Home health care” means care and treatment provided by a home
7 health agency and designed and supervised by a health care professional,
8 without which care and treatment a person would require admission to a
9 hospital or skilled nursing facility, as those terms are defined by Medicare
10 regulations. The care and treatment shall consist of one or more of the
11 following:
12 (A) Part-time or intermittent skilled nursing care.
13 (B) Physical therapy.
14 (C) Part-time or intermittent home health aide services that consist
15 primarily of caring for the patient.
16 (D) Medical supplies, drugs and equipment, and laboratory services
17 to the extent that laboratory services would have been covered if the patient
18 had been admitted to a hospital or skilled nursing facility. The medical
19 necessity of equipment may be reviewed by reference to the Medicare
20 guidelines for durable medical equipment.
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 114 of 181
1 (b)(1) A major medical insurance plan shall provide coverage for home
2 health care.
3 (2) A health insurer may require evidence of insurability as a
4 prerequisite to coverage.
5 (3) The coverage shall consist of at least 40 visits by a home health
6 agency in any calendar year, or in any continuous period of 12 months, for
7 each person covered under the health insurance plan.
8 (4) Each visit by a member of a home health care agency, other than a
9 home health aide, shall be considered one home health care visit, and four
10 hours of home health aide service shall be considered one home health care
11 visit. Coverage shall be provided for maternity and childbirth.
12 (c) Nothing in this section shall be deemed to require that home health care
13 coverage be provided to individuals eligible for Medicare.
14 (d) A health insurance plan shall not impose greater coinsurance, co-
15 payment, deductible, or other cost-sharing requirements for coverage of home
16 health care than apply to the diagnosis and treatment of any other physical or
17 mental condition under the plan.

5 § 4081. TOBACCO CESSATION
6 (a) As used in this section, “tobacco cessation medication” means all
7 therapies approved by the U.S. Food and Drug Administration for use in
8 tobacco cessation.

10 month supply per year of tobacco cessation medication, including over-the-
11 counter medication, if prescribed by a licensed health care professional for an
12 individual covered under the plan. A health insurance plan may require the
13 individual to pay the plan’s applicable prescription drug co-payment for the
14 tobacco cessation medication.
15 (c) This section shall apply to Medicaid and any other public health care
16 assistance program offered or administered by the State or by any subdivision
17 or instrumentality of the State.

3 § 4083. SERVICES FOR VICTIMS OF SEXUAL ASSAULT
4 (a) As used in this section, “sexual assault examination” means either or
5 both of the following:
6 (1) a physical examination of the patient, documentation of biological
7 and physical findings, and collection of evidence; and
8 (2) treatment of the patient’s injuries; providing care for sexually
9 transmitted infections; assessing pregnancy risk; discussing treatment options,
10 including reproductive health services, screening for the human
11 immunodeficiency virus, and prophylactic treatment when appropriate; and
12 providing instructions and referrals for follow-up care.
13 (b) A health insurance plan shall not impose any co-payment or
14 coinsurance or, to the extent permitted under federal law, deductible or other
15 cost-sharing requirement for the sexual assault examination of a victim of
16 alleged sexual assault for health care services associated with specific
17 procedure codes identified in a memorandum of understanding between the
18 health insurer and the Vermont Center for Crime Victim Services.

9 § 4093. RETAIL PHARMACIES; FILLING OF PRESCRIPTIONS
10 (a) A health insurer or pharmacy benefit manager doing business in

19 is within the lawful scope of practice of a pharmacist, the health insurer may

15 Subchapter 11. Prevention and Treatment of Cancer
16 § 4095a. COLORECTAL CANCER SCREENING
17 (a) As used in this section, “colonoscopy” means a procedure that enables
18 a health care professional to examine visually the inside of a patient’s entire
19 colon and includes the concurrent removal of polyps or biopsy, or both.
20 (b) A health insurance plan shall provide coverage for colorectal cancer
21 screening, including:
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 142 of 181
1 (1) for a covered individual who is not at high risk for colorectal cancer,
2 colorectal cancer screening examinations and laboratory tests in accordance
3 with the most recently published recommendations established by the U.S.
4 Preventive Services Task Force for average-risk individuals; and
5 (2) for a covered individual who is at high risk for colorectal cancer,
6 colorectal cancer screening examinations and laboratory tests as recommended
7 by the treating health care professional.
8 (c) For the purposes of subdivision (b)(2) of this section, an individual is at
9 high risk for colorectal cancer if the individual has:
10 (1) a family medical history of colorectal cancer or a genetic syndrome
11 predisposing the individual to colorectal cancer;
12 (2) a prior occurrence of colorectal cancer or precursor polyps;
13 (3) a prior occurrence of a chronic digestive disease condition such as
14 inflammatory bowel disease, Crohn’s disease, or ulcerative colitis; or
15 (4) other predisposing factors as determined by the individual’s treating
16 health care professional.
17 (d) Colorectal cancer screening services performed under contract with the
18 insurer shall not be subject to any co-payment, deductible, coinsurance, or
19 other cost-sharing requirement. In addition, a covered individual shall not be
20 subject to any additional charge for any service associated with a procedure or
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 143 of 181
1 test for colorectal cancer screening, which may include one or more of the
2 following:
3 (1) removal of tissue or other matter;
4 (2) laboratory services;
5 (3) health care professional services;
6 (4) facility use; and
7 (5) anesthesia.
8 § 4095b. MAMMOGRAPHY AND OTHER BREAST IMAGING
9 SERVICES
10 (a)(1) A health insurance plan shall provide coverage for screening
11 mammography and for other medically necessary breast imaging services upon
12 recommendation of a health care professional as needed to detect the presence
13 of breast cancer and other abnormalities of the breast or breast tissue. In
14 addition, a health insurance plan shall provide coverage for screening by
15 ultrasound or another appropriate imaging service for a covered individual for
16 whom the results of a screening mammogram were inconclusive or who has
17 dense breast tissue, or both.
18 (2) Benefits provided shall cover the full cost of the mammography,
19 ultrasound, and other breast imaging services and shall not be subject to any
20 co-payment, deductible, coinsurance, or other cost-sharing requirement or
21 additional charge, except to the extent that such coverage would disqualify a
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 144 of 181
1 high-deductible health plan from eligibility for a health savings account
2 pursuant to 26 U.S.C. § 223.
3 (b) This section shall apply only to procedures conducted by test facilities
4 accredited by the American College of Radiologists.
5 (c) As used in this section:
6 (1) “Mammography” means the x-ray examination of the breast using
7 equipment dedicated specifically for mammography, including the x-ray tube,
8 filter, compression device, and digital detector. The term includes breast
9 tomosynthesis.
10 (2) “Other breast imaging services” means diagnostic mammography,
11 ultrasound, and magnetic resonance imaging services that enable health care
12 professionals to detect the presence or absence of breast cancer and other
13 abnormalities affecting the breast or breast tissue.
14 (3) “Screening” includes the mammography or ultrasound test procedure
15 and a qualified health care professional’s interpretation of the results of the
16 procedure, including additional views and interpretation as needed.

16 (a) As used in this section:

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 149 of 181
1 (F) peer-reviewed abstracts accepted for presentation at major
2 medical association meetings.
3 (2) “Medically accepted indication” includes any use of a drug that has
4 been approved by the U.S. Food and Drug Administration and includes another
5 use of the drug if that use is prescribed by the covered individual’s health care
6 professional and supported by medical or scientific evidence.
7 (3) “Off-label use” means the prescription and use of drugs for
8 medically accepted indications other than those stated in the labeling approved
9 by the U.S. Food and Drug Administration.
10 (b) A health insurance plan shall provide coverage for off-label use in
11 cancer treatment in accordance with the following:
12 (1) A health insurance plan contract shall not exclude coverage for any
13 drug used for the treatment of cancer on grounds that the drug has not been
14 approved by the U.S. Food and Drug Administration, provided the use of the
15 drug is a medically accepted indication for the treatment of cancer.
16 (2) Coverage of a drug required by this section also includes medically
17 necessary services associated with the administration of the drug.
18 (3) This section shall not be construed to require coverage for a drug
19 when the U.S. Food and Drug Administration has determined its use to be
20 contraindicated for treatment of the current indication.
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 150 of 181
1 (4) A drug use that is covered under subdivision (1) of this subsection
2 shall not be denied coverage based on a “medical necessity” requirement
3 except for a reason unrelated to the legal status of the drug use.
4 (5) A health insurance plan that provides coverage of a drug as required
5 by this section may contain provisions for maximum benefits and coinsurance
6 and reasonable limitations, deductibles, and exclusions to the same extent these
7 provisions are applicable to coverage of all prescription drugs and are not
8 inconsistent with the requirements of this section.
9 (c) A determination by a health insurer that an off-label use of a
10 prescription drug under this section is not a medically accepted indication
11 supported by medical or scientific evidence is eligible for review under section
12 4063 of this title.
13 (d) This section shall apply to Medicaid and any other public health care

VT LEG #382889 v.1

1 the insurer or shall be covered in a manner consistent with out-of-network
2 provider reimbursement practices for primary care physicians; however, this
3 shall not relieve a health insurance plan from compliance with the applicable
4 network adequacy requirements adopted by the Commissioner by rule.
5 (d) Nothing contained in this section shall be construed as impeding or
6 preventing either the provision or the coverage of health care services by
7 licensed naturopathic physicians, within the lawful scope of naturopathic
8 practice, in hospital facilities on a staff or employee basis.
9 (e) This section shall apply to Medicaid and any other public health care
10 assistance program offered or administered by the State or by any subdivision
11 or instrumentality of the State.
12 § 4098d. COVERED SERVICES PROVIDED BY ATHLETIC TRAINERS
13 (a) To the extent a health insurance plan provides coverage for a particular
14 type of health care service or for any particular medical condition that is within
15 the scope of practice of athletic trainers, a licensed athletic trainer who acts
16 within the scope of practice authorized by 26 V.S.A. chapter 83 shall not be
17 denied reimbursement by the health insurance plan for those covered services
18 if the health insurance plan would reimburse another health care professional
19 for those services.
20 (b) Health care services provided by athletic trainers may be subject to
21 reasonable deductibles, co-payment and co-insurance amounts, fee or benefit
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 159 of 181
1 limits, practice parameters, and utilization review consistent with applicable
2 rules adopted by the Department of Financial Regulation, provided that the
3 amounts, limits, and review shall not function to direct treatment in a manner
4 unfairly discriminative against athletic trainer care, and collectively shall be
5 not more restrictive than those applicable under the same policy for care or
6 services provided by other health care professionals but allowing for the
7 management of the benefit consistent with variations in practice patterns and
8 treatment modalities among different types of health care professionals.
9 (c) A health insurer may require that the athletic trainer services be
10 provided by a licensed athletic trainer under contract with the insurer.
11 (d) Nothing in this section shall be construed as impeding or preventing
12 either the provision or coverage of health care services by licensed athletic
13 trainers within the lawful scope of athletic trainer practice.
14 § 4098e. CHOICE OF PROVIDERS FOR VISION CARE AND MEDICAL
15 EYE CARE SERVICES
16 (a) As used in this section:
17 (1) “Covered services” means services and materials for which
18 reimbursement from a vision care plan or other health insurance plan is
19 provided by a member’s or subscriber’s plan contract, or for which a
20 reimbursement would be available but for application of the deductible, co-
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 160 of 181
1 payment, or coinsurance requirements under the member’s or subscriber’s
2 health insurance plan.
3 (2) “Health insurance plan” has the same meaning as in section 4011 of
4 this chapter and also includes vision care plans.
5 (3) “Materials” includes lenses, devices containing lenses, prisms, lens
6 treatments and coatings, contact lenses, and prosthetic devices to correct,
7 relieve, or treat defects or abnormal conditions of the human eye or its adnexa.
8 (4) “Ophthalmologist” means a physician licensed pursuant to 26 V.S.A.
9 chapter 23 or an osteopathic physician licensed pursuant to 26 V.S.A. chapter
10 33 who has had special training in the field of ophthalmology.
11 (5) “Optician” means a person licensed pursuant to 26 V.S.A. chapter
12 47.
13 (6) “Optometrist” means a person licensed pursuant to 26 V.S.A.
14 chapter 30.
15 (7) “Vision care plan” means an integrated or stand-alone plan, policy,
16 or contract providing vision benefits to enrollees with respect to covered
17 services or covered materials, or both.
18 (b) To the extent a health insurance plan provides coverage for vision care
19 or medical eye care services, it shall cover those services whether provided by
20 a licensed optometrist or by a licensed ophthalmologist, provided the health
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 161 of 181
1 care professional is acting within the health care professional’s authorized
2 scope of practice and participates in the plan’s network.
3 (c) A health insurance plan shall impose no greater co-payment,
4 coinsurance, or other cost-sharing amount for services when provided by an
5 optometrist than for the same service when provided by an ophthalmologist.
6 (d) A health insurance plan shall provide to a licensed health care
7 professional acting within the health care professional’s scope of practice the
8 same level of reimbursement or other compensation for providing vision care
9 and medical eye care services that are within the lawful scope of practice of the
10 professions of medicine, optometry, and osteopathy, regardless of whether the
11 health care professional is an optometrist or an ophthalmologist.
12 (e)(1) A health insurer shall permit a licensed optometrist to participate in
13 plans or contracts providing for vision care or medical eye care to the same
14 extent as it does an ophthalmologist.
15 (2) A health insurer shall not require a licensed optometrist or
16 ophthalmologist to provide discounted materials benefits or to participate as a
17 provider in another health insurance or vision care plan or contract as a
18 condition or requirement for the optometrist’s or ophthalmologist’s
19 participation as a provider in any health insurance or vision care plan or
20 contract.

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 162 of 181
1 (f)(1) An agreement between a health insurer and an optometrist or
2 ophthalmologist for the provision of vision services to plan members or
3 subscribers in connection with coverage under a stand-alone vision care plan or
4 other health insurance plan shall not require that an optometrist or
5 ophthalmologist provide services or materials at a fee limited or set by the plan
6 or insurer unless the services or materials are reimbursed as covered services
7 under the contract.
8 (2) An optometrist or ophthalmologist shall not charge more for services
9 and materials that are noncovered services under a vision care plan or other
10 health insurance plan than the optometrist’s or ophthalmologist’s usual and
11 customary rate for those services and materials.
12 (3) Reimbursement paid by a vision care plan or other health insurance
13 plan for covered services and materials shall be reasonable and shall not
14 provide nominal reimbursement in order to claim that services and materials
15 are covered services.
16 (4)(A) A vision care plan or other health insurance plan shall not restrict
17 or otherwise limit, directly or indirectly, an optometrist’s, ophthalmologist’s,
18 or independent optician’s choice of or relationship with sources and suppliers

20 optometrist, ophthalmologist, or optician determines that the source, supplier,
21 or laboratory that the optometrist, ophthalmologist, or optician has selected
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 163 of 181
1 offers the products, services, or materials in a manner that is more beneficial to
2 the consumer, including with respect to cost, quality, timing, or selection, than
3 the source, supplier, or laboratory selected by the vision care plan or other
4 health insurance plan. The plan shall not impose any penalty or fee on an
5 optometrist, ophthalmologist, or independent optician for using any supplier,
6 optical laboratory, product, service, or material.
7 (B) The optometrist, ophthalmologist, or optician shall notify the
8 consumer of any additional costs the consumer may incur as the result of
9 procuring the products, services, or materials from the source, supplier, or
10 laboratory selected by the optometrist, ophthalmologist, or optician instead of
11 from the source, supplier, or laboratory selected by the vision care plan or
12 other health insurance plan.
13 (C) Nothing in this subdivision (4) shall be construed to prevent a
14 vision care plan or other health insurance plan from informing its policyholders
15 of the benefits available under the plan or from conducting an audit of an
16 optometrist’s, ophthalmologist’s, or optician’s use of alternative sources,
17 suppliers, or laboratories.
18 (D) The provisions of this subdivision (4) shall not apply to
19 Medicaid.

21 apply to Medicaid and any other public health care assistance program offered

19 § 4092.

6 (6) For purposes of As used in this section, “dependent coverage” shall

8 Sec. 31. ADDITIONAL CONFORMING REVISIONS
9 When preparing the Vermont Statutes Annotated for publication, the Office
10 of Legislative Counsel shall update any additional cross-references to statutes
11 in 8 V.S.A. chapter 107 that use the numbering scheme in effect prior to the
12 effective date of this act to conform to the new numbering scheme enacted by
13 this act.
14 * * * Interpretation and Rule Alignment * * *
15 Sec. 32. INTERPRETATION; RULE ALIGNMENT
16 (a) The purpose of this bill is to update and reorganize the health insurance
17 statutes. It is the intent of the General Assembly that the technical
18 amendments in this act shall not supersede substantive changes contained in
19 other bills enacted by the General Assembly during the current biennium.
20 Where possible, the amendments in this act shall be interpreted to be
21 supplemental to other amendments made to the sections of 8 V.S.A. chapter
VT LEG #382889 v.1
AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 181 of 181
1 107 using the numbering scheme in effect prior to the effective date of this act;
2 to the extent the provisions conflict, the substantive changes in other acts shall
3 take precedence over the technical changes in this act. Statutes added to or
4 amended in 8 V.S.A. chapter 107 that are enacted during the 2025–2026
5 biennium using the numbering scheme that existed prior to the effective date of
6 this act shall be codified in the corresponding statutes as renumbered by this
7 act.
8 (b) Rules adopted and orders, bulletins, forms, and guidance documents
9 issued by the Department of Financial Regulation, the Green Mountain Care
10 Board, and other State agencies that refer to statutes in 8 V.S.A. chapter 107
11 using the numbering that existed prior to the effective date of this act shall
12 continue to be valid following the effective date of this act until such time as
13 the relevant documents can be amended or updated to align with the
14 renumbering of that chapter by this act.
15 * * * Effective Date * * *
16 Sec. 33. EFFECTIVE DATE
17 This act shall take effect on September 1, 2025.

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 1 of 181
1 S.30
2 An act relating to updating and reorganizing the health insurance statutes in
3 8 V.S.A. chapter 107
4 It is hereby enacted by the General Assembly of the State of Vermont:
5 * * * Repeal of Existing 8 V.S.A. Chapter 107 * * *
6 Sec. 1. REPEAL OF EXISTING 8 V.S.A. CHAPTER 107
7 8 V.S.A. chapter 107 (health insurance) is repealed.
8 * * * Enactment of Updated and Reorganized 8 V.S.A. Chapter 107 * * *
9 Sec. 2. 8 V.S.A. chapter 107 is added to read:
10 CHAPTER 107. HEALTH INSURANCE
11 Subchapter 1. General Provisions
12 § 4011. DEFINITIONS
13 As used in this chapter:
14 (1) “Covered individual” means an individual who is covered by a
15 health insurance plan, whether as the primary subscriber or policyholder or as a
16 dependent, employee, or employee’s dependent under the plan.
17 (2) “Health care services” means services for the diagnosis, prevention,
18 treatment, cure, or relief of a health condition, illness, injury, or disease.
19 (3) “Health insurance plan” means a policy or contract issued by a
20 health insurer, including the health benefit plan or plans offered by the State of
21 Vermont to its employees and any health benefit plan offered by any agency or
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 2 of 181
1 instrumentality of the State to its employees. Unless otherwise specified,
2 “health insurance” does not include Vermont Medicaid.
3 (4) “Health insurer” means an insurance company that provides health
4 insurance as defined in subdivision 3301(a)(2) of this title, a nonprofit hospital
5 or medical service corporation, a managed care organization, a health
6 maintenance organization, and, to the extent permitted under federal law, any
7 administrator of an insured, self-insured, or publicly funded health care benefit
8 plan offered by a public or private entity.
9 (5) “Major medical insurance” means a comprehensive health insurance
10 plan that is not specific disease, accident, hospital indemnity, dental care,
11 vision care, disability income, long-term care, Medicare supplement insurance,
12 or other limited-benefit coverage. The term does not include short-term,
13 limited-duration health insurance coverage or a plan under which benefits are
14 paid directly to a covered individual or the individual’s assigns and for which
15 the amount of the benefit is not based on potential medical costs or on actual
16 costs incurred.
17 § 4012. COMPLIANCE WITH FEDERAL LAW
18 (a) Except as otherwise provided in this title, health insurers, hospital and
19 medical service corporations, and health maintenance organizations that issue,
20 sell, renew, or offer health insurance plans in Vermont shall comply with the
21 requirements of the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act of
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 3 of 181
1 1996, as amended from time to time (42 U.S.C. Chapter 6A, Subchapter
2 XXV), and the Patient Protection and Affordable Care Act of 2010, Pub. L.
3 No. 111-148, as amended by the Health Care and Education Reconciliation Act
4 of 2010, Pub. L. No. 111-152. The Commissioner shall enforce such
5 requirements pursuant to the Commissioner’s authority under this title.
6 (b)(1) Health insurers, hospital and medical service corporations, health
7 maintenance organizations, and health care providers, as that term is defined in
8 18 V.S.A. § 9432, shall comply with the requirements of the No Surprises Act,
9 Pub. L. No. 116-260, Division BB, Title I, as amended from time to time.
10 (2) The Commissioner shall enforce the requirements of the No
11 Surprises Act as they apply to health insurers, hospital and medical service
12 corporations, health maintenance organizations, and health care providers, to
13 the extent permitted under federal law, pursuant to the Commissioner’s
14 authority under this title. The Commissioner may also refer cases of
15 noncompliance to the U.S. Department of Health and Human Services under
16 the terms of a collaborative enforcement agreement, or to the Office of the
17 Vermont Attorney General.
18 § 4013. DISCRIMINATION PROHIBITED
19 No health insurer shall make or permit any unfair discrimination between
20 individuals of substantially the same hazard in the amount of premium rates
21 charged for any health insurance plan or in the benefits payable under the plan;

1 provided, however, that this section shall not be construed to prohibit different
2 premium rates, different benefits, or different underwriting procedure for

4 § 4014. ADVERTISING PRACTICES
5 (a) No company doing business in this State, and no insurance agent or
6 broker, shall use in connection with the solicitation of health insurance or
7 pharmacy benefit management any advertising copy or advertising practice or
8 any plan of solicitation that is materially misleading or deceptive. An
9 advertising copy or advertising practice or plan of solicitation shall be
10 considered to be materially misleading or deceptive if by implication or
11 otherwise it transmits information in such manner or of such substance that a
12 prospective applicant for health insurance may be misled by it to the
13 applicant’s material damage.
14 (b)(1) If the Commissioner finds that any such advertising copy or
15 advertising practice or plan of solicitation is materially misleading or
16 deceptive, the Commissioner shall order the company or the agent or broker
17 using such copy or practice or plan to cease and desist from such use.
18 (2) Before making any such finding and order, the Commissioner shall
19 give notice, not less than 10 days in advance, and a hearing to the company,
20 agent, or broker affected.
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 5 of 181
1 (3) If the Commissioner finds, after due notice and hearing, that any
2 authorized insurer, licensed pharmacy benefit manager, licensed insurance
3 agent, or licensed insurance broker has intentionally violated any such order to
4 cease and desist, the Commissioner may suspend or revoke the license of such
5 insurer, pharmacy benefit manager, agent, or broker.
6 § 4015. PENALTIES FOR VIOLATIONS
7 The Commissioner may impose an administrative penalty of up to $750.00
8 on any person who intentionally violates any provision of this chapter or any
9 order of the Commissioner made in accordance with this chapter. The
10 Commissioner may also suspend or revoke the license of a health insurer or
11 agent for any such intentional violation.
12 § 4016. APPEAL
13 (a) Any person aggrieved by any action of the Commissioner may obtain a
14 review by appeal to the Superior Court of Washington County. The appeal
15 shall be based on the record of the proceedings before the Commissioner and
16 shall not be limited to questions of law. If the appeal is from an order of the
17 Commissioner, the order shall not take effect during the pendency of the
18 appeal unless the court determines otherwise.
19 (b) The court may review all the facts and in disposing of any issue before
20 it may modify, affirm, or reverse any order of the Commissioner in whole or in
21 part.
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 6 of 181
1 (c) Either party may appeal from the decision of the Superior Court to the
2 Supreme Court in the manner provided by law.
3 § 4017. EXEMPTION FROM ATTACHMENT AND TRUSTEE PROCESS
4 So much of any benefits under all policies of health insurance as does not
5 exceed $200.00 for each month during any period of disability covered by the
6 policy shall not be liable to attachment, trustee process, or other process, or to
7 be seized, taken, appropriated, or applied by any legal or equitable process or
8 by operation of law, either before or after payment of such benefits, to pay any
9 debt or liabilities of the person insured under the policy. However, this
10 exemption shall not apply where an action is brought to recover for necessaries
11 contracted for during the period of disability and the writ or bill of complaint
12 contains a statement to that effect. When a policy provides for a lump sum
13 payment because of a dismemberment or other loss insured, the payment shall
14 be exempt from execution of the covered individual’s creditors.
15 § 4018. THIRD-PARTY OWNERSHIP
16 Nothing in this chapter shall be construed as preventing a person other than
17 the covered individual with proper insurable interest from making application
18 for and owning a policy covering the covered individual or from being entitled
19 under such a policy to any indemnities, benefits, and rights provided in the
20 policy.

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 7 of 181
1 § 4019. NOTICE AS WAIVER
2 A health insurer shall not be deemed to have waived any rights to defend a
3 claim under a health insurance plan based solely on the health insurer’s
4 acknowledgement of receipt of notice under the plan, furnishing or accepting
5 forms for filing proof of loss under the plan, or investigating any claim of loss
6 under the plan.
7 § 4020. AGE LIMITS
8 (a) If a health insurance plan contains a provision establishing, as an age
9 limit or otherwise, a date after which the coverage provided by the plan will
10 not be effective, and if that date falls within a period for which the health
11 insurer has accepted a premium or if the health insurer accepts a premium after
12 that date, the coverage provided by the plan shall continue in force subject to
13 any right of cancellation until the end of the period for which a premium has
14 been accepted.
15 (b) Notwithstanding any provision of subsection (a) of this section to the
16 contrary, if the age of the covered individual has been misstated and if,
17 according to the correct age of the covered individual, the coverage provided
18 by the policy would not have become effective or would have ceased prior to
19 the health insurer’s acceptance of the premium or premiums, then the health
20 insurer’s liability shall be limited to the refund, upon request, of all premiums
21 paid for the period not covered by the plan.

1 § 4021. TERMINATION OF COVERAGE
2 (a)(1) A major medical insurance policy issued by a health insurer that
3 insures employees, members, or subscribers for hospital and medical insurance
4 on an expense-incurred, service, or prepaid basis shall:
5 (A) provide notice to the policyholder or other responsible party of
6 any premium payment due on a policy at least 21 days before the due date; and
7 (B) provide a grace period of at least one month for the payment of
8 each premium falling due after the first premium, during which grace period
9 the plan shall continue in force and the issuer of the plan shall be liable for
10 valid claims for covered losses incurred prior to the end of the grace period.
11 (2) If the issuer of a plan described subdivision (1) of this subsection
12 does not receive payment by the due date, the issuer shall send a termination
13 notice to the policyholder at least 21 days prior to termination notifying the
14 policyholder that the issuer may terminate the plan if payment is not received
15 by the termination date.
16 (3) The termination date of a plan described in subdivision (1) of this
17 subsection shall not be earlier than the day following the last day of the grace
18 period set forth in subdivision (1)(A) of this subsection.
19 (b) For all health insurance policies other than major medical insurance
20 policies, a health insurer shall notify a policyholder of any premium payment
21 due on a policy at least 21 days before the due date. If a health insurer does
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 9 of 181
1 not receive payment by the due date, the health insurer shall send a termination
2 notice to the policyholder notifying the policyholder that the health insurer will
3 terminate the policy effective on the due date if payment is not received within
4 14 days from the date of mailing of the termination notice. If a health insurer
5 does not receive payment within 14 days from the date of mailing of the
6 termination notice, the health insurer may cancel coverage effective on the due
7 date.

3 § 4028. FORM AND CONTENTS OF POLICY
4 No policy of individual health insurance shall be delivered or issued for
5 delivery to any person in this State unless all of the following conditions are
6 met:
7 (1) The policy sets forth all of the monetary and other considerations for
8 the policy.
9 (2) The policy sets forth the time at which the insurance takes effect and
10 terminates.
11 (3) The policy purports to insure only one person, except that a policy
12 may insure, originally or by subsequent amendment, upon the application of an
13 adult member of a family who shall be deemed the policyholder, any two or
14 more eligible members of that family, including a spouse or civil union
15 partner, dependent children or any children under a specified age that shall not
16 exceed 26 years of age, and any other person dependent upon the policyholder.
17 (4) The style, arrangement, and overall appearance of the policy give no
18 undue prominence to any portion of the text, and every printed portion of the
19 text of the policy and of any endorsements or attached papers is plainly printed
20 in light-faced type of a style in general use, the size of which shall be uniform
21 and not less than 10-point with a lowercase unspaced alphabet length not less
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 25 of 181
1 than 120-point. As used in this subdivision, the “text” includes all printed
2 matter except the name and address of the insurer; the name or title of the
3 policy; the brief description, if any; and the captions and subcaptions.
4 (5) The exceptions and reductions of indemnity are set forth in the
5 policy and, except those that are set forth in sections 4029 and 4030 of this
6 title, are printed, at the insurer’s option, either with the benefit provision to

11 § 4031. OMISSION OF INAPPLICABLE OR INCONSISTENT
12 STANDARD PROVISIONS
13 If any provision of sections 4029 and 4030 of this title is in whole or in part
14 inapplicable to or inconsistent with the coverage provided by a particular form
15 of policy, the health insurer, with the approval of the Commissioner, shall omit
16 from such policy any inapplicable provision or part of a provision, and shall
17 modify any inconsistent provision or part of the provision in such manner as to
18 make the provision as contained in the policy consistent with the coverage
19 provided by the policy.

1 § 4032. ORDER OF STANDARD POLICY PROVISIONS
2 The provisions specified in sections 4029 and 4030 of this title, or any
3 corresponding provisions used in lieu of those provisions as permitted by those
4 sections, shall either be printed in the same order as the provisions are set forth
5 in those sections or, at the option of the health insurer, any such provision may
6 appear as a unit in any part of the policy, with other provisions to which it may
7 be logically related, provided the resulting policy shall not be in whole or in
8 part unintelligible, uncertain, ambiguous, abstruse, or likely to mislead a
9 person to whom the policy is offered, delivered, or issued.
10 § 4033. DISCRETIONARY CLAUSES PROHIBITED
11 (a) The purpose of this section is to ensure that health insurance benefits,
12 disability income protection coverage, and life insurance benefits are
13 contractually guaranteed and to avoid the conflict of interest that may occur
14 when the carrier responsible for providing benefits has discretionary authority
15 to decide what benefits are due. Nothing in this section shall be construed to
16 impose any requirement or duty on any person other than a health insurer or a
17 health insurer offering disability income protection coverage or life insurance.
18 (b) As used in this section:
19 (1) “Disability income protection coverage” means a policy, contract,
20 certificate, or agreement that provides for weekly, monthly, or other periodic
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 44 of 181
1 payments for a specified period during the continuance of disability resulting
2 from illness, injury, or a combination of illness and injury.
3 (2) “Health insurer” has the same meaning as in section 4021 of this
4 chapter and, as used in this section, also includes entities offering policies for
5 specific disease, accident, injury, hospital indemnity, dental care, disability
6 income, long-term care, and other limited benefit coverage.
7 (3) “Life insurance” means a policy, contract, certificate, or agreement
8 that provides life insurance as defined in subdivision 3301(a)(1) of this title.
9 (c) No policy, contract, certificate, or agreement offered or issued in this
10 State by a health insurer to provide, deliver, arrange for, pay for, or reimburse
11 any of the costs of health care services may contain a provision purporting to
12 reserve discretion to the health insurer to interpret the terms of the contract or
13 to provide standards of interpretation or review that are inconsistent with the
14 laws of this State, and any such provision in a policy, contract, certificate, or
15 agreement shall be null and void.
16 (d) No policy, contract, certificate, or agreement offered or issued in this
17 State providing for disability income protection coverage may contain a
18 provision purporting to reserve discretion to the insurer to interpret the terms
19 of the contract or to provide standards of interpretation or review that are
20 inconsistent with the laws of this State, and any such provision in a policy,
21 contract, certificate, or agreement shall be null and void.
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 45 of 181
1 (e) No policy, contract, certificate, or agreement of life insurance offered or
2 issued in this State shall contain a provision purporting to reserve discretion to
3 the insurer to interpret the terms of the contract or to provide standards of
4 interpretation or review that are inconsistent with the laws of this State, and
5 any such provision in a policy, contract, certificate, or agreement shall be null
6 and void.
7 § 4034. REQUIREMENTS OF OTHER JURISDICTIONS
8 (a) Any policy of a foreign or alien insurer, when delivered or issued for
9 delivery to any person in this State, may contain any provision that is not less
10 favorable to the covered individual than the provisions of this chapter and that
11 is prescribed or required by the law of the state under which the insurer is
12 organized.
13 (b) Any policy of a domestic health insurer, when issued for delivery in any
14 other state or country, may contain any provision permitted or required by the
15 laws of such other state or country.
16 § 4035. POLICIES NOT AFFECTED

18 this title shall apply to or affect:
19 (1) any policy of workers’ compensation insurance or any policy of
20 liability insurance, with or without supplementary coverage;

2 (3) any blanket or group policy of insurance enumerated in sections

4 sections; or
5 (4) life insurance, endowment, or annuity contracts, or contracts
6 supplemental to those contracts, that contain only such provisions relating to
7 accident and sickness insurance as:
8 (A) provide additional benefits in case of death or dismemberment or
9 loss of sight by accident; or
10 (B) operate to safeguard the contracts against lapse or to give a
11 special surrender value or special benefit or an annuity in the event that the
12 insured or annuitant becomes totally and permanently disabled, as defined by
13 the contract or supplemental contract.
14 § 4036. NONCONFORMING POLICIES
15 (a) A health insurance policy shall not contain any provision that makes the
16 policy or any portion of the policy less favorable in any respect to the covered
17 individual than the provisions of the policy that are regulated by sections 4029
18 and 4030 of this title.
19 (b) A policy delivered or issued for delivery to any person in this State in
20 violation of sections 4029 and 4030 of this title shall be held valid but shall be
21 construed as provided in this chapter. When any provision in a policy
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 47 of 181
1 regulated by sections 4029 and 4030 is in conflict with any provision of those
2 sections, the rights, duties, and obligations of the health insurer and the
3 covered individual shall be governed by the provisions of those sections.
4 § 4037. APPLICATIONS FOR INSURANCE
5 (a)(1) A covered individual shall not be bound by any statement made in an
6 application for a policy unless a copy of the application is attached to or
7 endorsed on the policy as a part of the policy when issued.
8 (2) If a policy delivered or issued for delivery to any person in this State
9 is reinstated or renewed and the covered individual or assignee of the policy
10 makes a written request to the health insurer for a copy of the application, if
11 any, for such reinstatement or renewal, the health insurer shall deliver or mail a
12 copy of the application to the individual making the request within 15 days
13 after the receipt of the request. If the health insurer does not deliver or mail the
14 copy within 15 days, the health insurer shall be precluded from introducing the
15 application as evidence in any action or proceeding based on or involving the
16 policy or its reinstatement or renewal.
17 (b) No alteration of a written application for a policy shall be made by any
18 person other than the applicant without the applicant’s written consent, except
19 that insertions may be made by the health insurer, for administrative purposes
20 only, in a manner that indicates clearly that the insertions are not to be ascribed
21 to the applicant.
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 48 of 181
1 (c) The falsity of any statement in an application for a policy shall not bar
2 the right to recovery under the policy unless the false statement materially
3 affected either the acceptance of the risk or the hazard assumed by the health
4 insurer.
5 § 4038. RULEMAKING ON POLICY FILINGS
6 The Commissioner may adopt such reasonable rules concerning the
7 procedure for the filing or submission of policies subject to sections 4023 and
8 4028–4030 of this title as are necessary, proper, or advisable for the
9 administration of these sections. This provision shall not abridge any other
10 authority granted to the Commissioner by law.

4 § 4042. GROUP INSURANCE POLICIES; REQUIRED POLICY
5 PROVISIONS
6 (a) Terms and conditions. No group health insurance policy shall contain
7 any provision relating to notice of claim, proofs of loss, time of payment of
8 claims, or time within which legal action must be brought upon the policy that,
9 in the opinion of the Commissioner, is less favorable to the persons insured
10 than would be permitted by the provisions set forth in section 4029 of this title.
11 In addition, each such policy shall contain in substance the following
12 provisions:
13 (1) A provision that the policy; the application of the policyholder, if an
14 application or copy is attached to the policy; and the individual applications, if
15 any, submitted by the employees or members in connection with the policy
16 shall constitute the entire contract between the parties, and that all statements,
17 in the absence of fraud, made by any applicant or applicants shall be deemed
18 representations and not warranties, and that no such statement shall avoid the
19 insurance or reduce benefits under the policy unless contained in a written
20 application, of which a copy is attached to the policy.
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 54 of 181
1 (2) A provision that the health insurer will furnish to the policyholder,
2 for delivery to each employee or member of the insured group, an individual
3 certificate setting forth in summary form a statement of the essential features
4 of the insurance coverage of the employee or member and to whom benefits
5 are payable under the policy. If dependents are included in the coverage, only
6 one certificate need be issued for each family unit.
7 (3) A provision that to the group originally insured may be added from
8 time to time eligible new employees or members or dependents, as the case
9 may be, in accordance with the terms of the policy.
10 (4) A provision that the health insurer shall not exclude part-time
11 employees and shall offer the same group health benefits to part-time
12 employees as it offers to the employee groups of which the part-time
13 employees would be members if they were full-time employees. The health
14 insurer shall offer to include the part-time employees as part of the employer’s
15 employee group, at the full rate to be paid by the employer and the employee,
16 at a rate prorated between the employer and the employee, or at the employee’s
17 expense. As used in this subdivision, “part-time employee” means any
18 employee who works a minimum of at least 17.5 hours per week.

13 Subchapter 4. Continuation and Conversion of
14 Group Health Insurance Policies
15 § 4047a. CONTINUATION OF GROUP
16 (a) All group major medical insurance and dental insurance policies shall
17 provide that any person whose insurance under the group policy would
18 terminate because of the occurrence of a qualifying event as defined in
19 subsection (b) of this section shall be entitled to continue the person’s health
20 insurance under that group policy.
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 59 of 181
1 (b) For purposes of this subchapter, “qualifying event” means:
2 (1) loss of employment, including a reduction in hours that results in
3 ineligibility for employer-sponsored coverage;
4 (2) divorce, dissolution, or legal separation of the covered employee
5 from the employee’s spouse or civil union partner;
6 (3) a dependent child ceasing to qualify as a dependent child under the
7 generally applicable requirements of the policy; or
8 (4) death of the covered employee or member.
9 (c) The provisions of this section shall not apply if one or more of the
10 following conditions applies:
11 (1) The deceased person or employee was not insured under the group
12 policy on the date of the qualifying event.
13 (2) The person is covered by Medicare.
14 (3) The person is covered by any other group insured or uninsured
15 arrangement that provides dental coverage or hospital and medical coverage
16 for individuals in a group and under which the person was not covered
17 immediately prior to the qualifying event, and no preexisting condition
18 exclusion applies; provided, however, that the person shall remain eligible for
19 continuation coverages that are not available under the insured or uninsured
20 arrangement.
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 60 of 181
1 (4) The person has a loss of employment due to misconduct as defined
2 in 21 V.S.A. § 1344.
3 (d) The continuation required by this section only applies to major medical
4 insurance and dental insurance benefits.
5 (e) Notice of the continuation privilege shall be included in each certificate
6 of coverage and shall be provided by the employer to the employee within 30
7 days following the occurrence of any qualifying event.
8 § 4047b. CONTINUATION; NOTICE; TERMS
9 (a) A person electing continuation shall notify the health insurer, or the
10 policyholder, or the contractor, or agent for the group if the policyholder did
11 not contract for the policy directly with the health insurer, of such election in
12 writing within 60 days after receiving notice following the occurrence of a
13 qualifying event pursuant to subsection 4047a(e) of this title. Notice of
14 election to continue under the group policy shall be accompanied by the initial
15 contribution, which shall include payment for the period from the qualifying
16 event through the end of the month in which the election is made.
17 (b) Contributions shall be due on a monthly basis in advance to the health
18 insurer or the health insurer’s agent, and shall not be more than 102 percent of
19 the group rate for the insurance being continued under the group policy on the
20 due date of each payment.

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30

1 § 4047c. TERMINATION OF COVERAGE

8 contribution.
9 (3) The person is covered by Medicare.
10 (4) The person is covered by any other group insured or uninsured

VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 63 of 181

2 group.

6 subchapter.
7 § 4048b. TERMINATION FOR NONPAYMENT OF PREMIUM OR
8 SUBSCRIPTION CHARGES
9 (a) If a group health insurance policy or subscriber contract provides for
10 automatic termination of the policy or contract after a premium or subscription
11 charge has remained unpaid through the grace period allowed for such
12 payment, the health insurer shall be liable for valid claims for covered losses
13 incurred prior to the end of the grace period.
14 (b) If the actions of the health insurer after the end of the grace period
15 indicate that it considers the policy or contract to be continuing in force beyond
16 the end of the grace period, including actions such as continuing to recognize
17 claims subsequently incurred, the health insurer shall be liable for valid claims
18 for losses incurred prior to the effective date of written notice of termination to
19 the policyholder or other entity responsible for making payments or submitting
20 subscription charges to the health insurer.
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 64 of 181
1 (c) The health insurer shall notify a policyholder or other responsible entity
2 of any premium payment due on a policy at least 21 days before the due date.
3 The effective date of termination of a policy or contract shall not be prior to
4 midnight at the end of the 14th day following mailing of notice of termination.
5 § 4048c. NOTICE OF TERMINATION
6 (a) A notice of termination of a health insurer’s group health insurance
7 policy or subscriber contract shall:
8 (1) request the group policyholder or other entity involved to notify
9 employees or members covered under the policy or subscriber contract of the
10 date of termination of the policy or contract and to advise the employees or
11 members that, unless otherwise provided in the policy or contract, the health
12 insurer shall not be liable for claims for losses incurred after such date; and
13 (2) advise, in any instance in which the plan involves employee
14 contributions, that if the policyholder or other entity continues to collect
15 contributions for the coverage beyond the date of termination, the policyholder
16 or other entity may be held solely liable for the benefits with respect to which
17 the contributions have been collected.
18 (b) The health insurer giving notice of termination shall prepare and furnish
19 to the policyholder or other entity at the time of notice a supply of a notice
20 form to be distributed to covered employees or members. The form shall state
21 the fact of termination and the effective date of termination. The form shall
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 65 of 181
1 contain a statement directing employees or members to refer to their
2 certificates or contracts in order to determine their rights.
3 § 4048d. EXTENSION OF BENEFITS
4 (a) Each group health insurance policy or subscriber contract shall provide
5 a reasonable extension of benefits in the event that the employer or member is
6 in a condition of total disability on the date of termination of the group policy
7 or contract in accordance with the provisions of this section.
8 (b) A policy or contract providing benefits for loss of time from work or
9 specific indemnity during hospital confinement shall provide that termination
10 of the policy or contract during a loss of time or confinement shall have no
11 effect on benefits payable for the loss of time or confinement.
12 (c) A policy or contract providing hospital or medical expense coverage
13 benefits shall provide an extension of benefits of at least 12 months under
14 major medical insurance coverage and at least 90 days under other types of
15 hospital or medical expense coverage.
16 (d) The provisions of a policy or contract relating to extension of benefits
17 or accrued liability shall be described in the policy or contract as well as in
18 group insurance certificates. The benefits payable during a period of extension
19 or accrued liability may be subject to the policy’s or contract’s regular benefit
20 limits.

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 66 of 181
1 (e) Nothing in this section shall be construed to require an extension of
2 dental benefits.
3 § 4048e. REPLACEMENT COVERAGE
4 (a) General. When the group health insurance policy or subscriber contract
5 of a health insurer replaces a policy or contract providing similar benefits of
6 another health insurer, the liability of both health insurers shall be as provided
7 in this section and rules adopted pursuant to this section.
8 (b) Liability of prior health insurer. A prior health insurer remains liable
9 after termination of its policy or contract only to the extent of its accrued
10 liabilities and extensions of benefits.
11 (c) Liability of succeeding health insurer.
12 (1) A succeeding health insurer shall offer a group health insurance
13 policy or subscriber contract to replace a prior health insurer’s policy or
14 contract in accordance with the provisions of this subsection.
15 (2) A succeeding health insurer shall offer a policy or contract to cover
16 all persons who:
17 (A) are covered or are a member of a class eligible for coverage
18 under the prior health insurer’s policy or contract on the date of termination of
19 the prior health insurer’s policy or contract; or
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 67 of 181
1 (B) are a member of a class eligible for coverage under the
2 succeeding health insurer’s policy or contract on the date of termination of the
3 prior health insurer’s policy or contract.
4 (3) The succeeding health insurer is not liable under this subsection for
5 benefits required to be paid by the prior health insurer.
6 (4) When replacing a prior health insurer’s plan that is not subject to
7 section 4048d of this title, the succeeding health insurer shall, in addition to the
8 coverage required to be offered under subdivision (2) of this subsection, offer a
9 policy or contract that provides a level of benefit equal to the lesser of:
10 (A) the extension of benefits that would have been required if the
11 prior health insurer’s policy or contract was subject to section 4048d of this
12 title; or
13 (B) the extension of benefits required for the succeeding health
14 insurer’s policy or contract, except that any such benefits may be reduced by
15 benefits actually payable under the prior health insurer’s plan.
16 (5) The preexisting condition limitation of a succeeding health insurer’s
17 policy or contract shall provide a level of benefits equal to the lesser of:
18 (A) the benefits of the succeeding health insurer’s policy or contract
19 determined without application of the preexisting conditions limitation; or
20 (B) the benefits of the prior health insurer’s policy or contract.
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 68 of 181
1 (6) The succeeding health insurer, in applying a deductible or waiting-
2 period provision in its policy or contract, shall give credit for the satisfaction of
3 the same or similar provisions under the prior health insurer’s policy or
4 contract.
5 (7) At the succeeding health insurer’s request, the prior health insurer
6 shall furnish all information needed to determine the benefits available under
7 the prior health insurer’s policy or contract.
8 (d) Rules. The Commissioner shall adopt rules necessary to carry out the
9 purposes of this section.
