2 (b) Premium increases.
3 (1) Within five days after receiving a request for approval of any
4 composite average rate increase in excess of three percent, or any other
5 coverage changes that the Commissioner determines will have a comparable
6 impact on cost or availability of coverage for a Medicare supplement insurance
7 policy issued by any health insurer with 5,000 or more total lives in the
8 Vermont Medicare supplement insurance market, the Commissioner shall
9 notify the Department of Disabilities, Aging, and Independent Living of the
10 proposed premium increase. A composite average rate is the enrollment-
11 weighted average rate increase of all plans offered by a health insurer.
12 (2) Within five days after receiving notification pursuant to subdivision
13 (1) of this subsection, the Department of Disabilities, Aging, and Independent
14 Living shall inform the members of the Advisory Board established pursuant to
15 33 V.S.A. § 505 of the proposed premium increase.
16 (3)(A) The Commissioner shall not approve any request to increase
17 Medicare supplement insurance premium rates unless the amount of the rate
18 increase complies with the statutory standards for approval under sections
19 4026, 4513, 4584, and 5104 of this title. Any approved rate increase shall not
20 be based on an unreasonable change in loss ratio from the previous year, unless
21 the Commissioner makes written findings that such change is necessary to
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 70 of 181
1 prevent a substantial adverse impact on the financial condition of the health
2 insurer. In acting on such rate increase requests, the Commissioner may deny
3 the request, approve the rate increase as requested, or approve a rate increase in
4 an amount different from the increase requested. A decision by the
5 Commissioner other than an approval of the rate requested may be appealed by
6 the health insurer, provided that the burden of proof shall be on the health
7 insurer to show that the approved rate does not meet the statutory standards
8 established under this subsection.
9 (B) Before acting on the rate increase requested, the Commissioner
10 may make such examination or investigation as the Commissioner deems
11 necessary, including where applicable the review process set forth in
12 subdivision (C) of this subdivision (3).
13 (C)(i) In reviewing any Medicare supplement insurance rate increase

VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 71 of 181
1 testimony and will be available to answer questions of the Commissioner and

6 § 4052. BLANKET HEALTH INSURANCE
7 (a) Blanket health insurance is a form of health insurance that, to the extent
8 permitted under federal law, is supplemental to major medical health insurance
9 or provides coverage other than the payment of all or a portion of the cost of
10 health care services or products, and that covers special groups of persons as
11 follows:
12 (1) under a policy or contract issued to any common carrier, which shall
13 be deemed the policyholder, covering a group defined as all persons who may
14 become passengers on such common carrier;
15 (2) under a policy or contract issued to an employer, who shall be
16 deemed the policyholder, covering any group of employees defined by
17 reference to exceptional hazards incident to such employment;
18 (3) under a policy or contract issued to a public school, independent
19 school, or approved education program, as those terms are defined in
20 16 V.S.A. § 11; to a postsecondary school, as defined in 16 V.S.A.
21 § 176(b)(1); or to a prequalified private prekindergarten provider, as defined in
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 74 of 181
1 16 V.S.A. § 829(a)(3), or to the head or principal of the school, program, or
2 provider, who or which shall be deemed the policyholder, covering students or
3 teachers, or both;
4 (4) under a policy or contract issued in the name of any volunteer fire
5 department, emergency medical services provider, or other such volunteer
6 group, which shall be deemed the policyholder, covering all of the members of
7 the department or group in connection with their department or group
8 activities; or
9 (5) under a policy or contract issued to any other substantially similar
10 group that, in the discretion of the Commissioner and after the prior approval
11 by the Commissioner of the group, may be subject to the issuance of a blanket
12 health policy or contract.
13 (b)(1) No blanket health insurance policy shall contain any provision
14 relating to notice of claim, proofs of loss, time of payment of claims, or time
15 within which legal action must be brought upon the policy that, in the opinion
16 of the Commissioner, is less favorable to the persons insured than would be
17 permitted by the provisions set forth in section 4029 of this title.
18 (2) An individual application shall not be required from a person
19 covered under a blanket health policy or contract, nor shall it be necessary for
20 the insurer to furnish each person a certificate.
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 75 of 181
1 (3) All benefits under any blanket health policy shall, unless for hospital
2 and physician service or surgical benefits, be payable to the person insured, or
3 to the person’s designated beneficiary or beneficiaries, or to the person’s
4 estate, except that if the person insured is a minor, the benefits may be made
5 payable to the minor’s parent, guardian, or other person actually supporting the
6 minor.
7 (4) Nothing in this section shall be deemed to affect the legal liability of
8 policyholders for the death of, or injury to, any members of the group.
9 (c) No blanket health insurance policy that provides coverage for the
10 payment of all or a portion of the cost of health care services or products shall
11 contain any provision that does not comply with a requirement of this title, or a
12 rule adopted pursuant to this title applicable to health insurance, other than
13 those requirements applicable to nongroup health insurance or small group
14 health insurance. The Commissioner may waive the application to a blanket
15 insurance policy of one or more of the health insurance requirements of this
16 title, or a rule adopted pursuant to this title, if the requirement is not relevant to
17 the types of risks and duration of risks insured against in the blanket insurance
18 policy.
19 § 4053. SHORT-TERM, LIMITED-DURATION HEALTH INSURANCE
20 (a) As used in this section, “short-term, limited-duration health insurance”

VT LEG #382889 v.1

2025 Page 76 of 181
1 expense benefits coverage pursuant to a policy or contract with a health insurer

6 health insurance in this State unless the person is exempted by subdivision

18 consumer protections that are and are not included. The Commissioner shall
19 determine the specific disclosure language that shall be used in all short-term,
20 limited-duration health insurance policies, contracts, and application materials

1 § 4057. COVERAGE OF CHILDREN
2 (a) Definition. “Health insurance plan” has the same meaning as in section
3 4011 of this chapter and shall be subject to the same excepted benefits, in each
4 case, as set forth in 45 C.F.R. § 146.145, as in effect as of December 31, 2017.
5 (b) Newborn coverage.
6 (1) A health insurance plan that provides dependent coverage of
7 children shall also provide that health insurance benefits applicable to children
8 are payable with respect to a newly born child of the insured or subscriber
9 from the moment of birth. Coverage for a newly born child shall include
10 coverage of injury, sickness, and necessary care and treatment of medically
11 diagnosed congenital defect or birth abnormality.
12 (2) Coverage for a newly born child shall be provided without notice or
13 additional premium for not less than 60 days after the date of birth. If payment
14 of a specific premium or subscription fee is required in order to have the
15 coverage continue beyond such 60-day period, the policy may require that
16 notification of the birth of the newly born child and payment of the required
17 premium or fees be furnished to the health insurer within a period of not less
18 than 60 days after the date of birth.
19 (c) Adopted child coverage.
20 (1) As used in this section:
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 79 of 181
1 (A) “Child” means, in connection with any adoption or placement for
2 adoption of the child, an individual who has not attained 18 years of age as of
3 the date of the adoption or placement for adoption.
4 (B) “Placement for adoption” means the assumption and retention by
5 a person of a legal obligation for total or partial support of a child in
6 anticipation of the adoption of the child. The child’s placement with a person
7 terminates upon the termination of such legal obligations.
8 (2) In any case in which a health insurance plan provides coverage for
9 dependent children of covered individuals, the plan shall provide benefits to
10 dependent children placed with covered individuals for adoption under the
11 same terms and conditions as apply to the natural, dependent children of the
12 covered individuals, irrespective of whether the adoption has become final.
13 (3) A health insurance plan shall not restrict coverage under the plan of
14 any dependent child adopted by a covered individual, or placed with a covered
15 individual for adoption, solely on the basis of a preexisting condition of the
16 child at the time that the child would otherwise become eligible for coverage
17 under the plan, if the adoption or placement for adoption occurs while the
18 covered individual is eligible for coverage under the plan.
19 (d) Coverage required until 26 years of age. A health insurance plan that
20 provides dependent coverage of children shall continue to make that coverage
21 available for an adult child until the child attains 26 years of age, provided that
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 80 of 181
1 this subsection shall not apply to a plan providing coverage for a specified
2 disease or other limited benefit coverage, and further provided that nothing in
3 this subsection shall require a plan to make coverage available for the child of
4 a child receiving dependent coverage.
5 (e) Coverage of adult child with a disability.
6 (1) A health insurance plan that provides for terminating the coverage of
7 a dependent child upon attainment of the limiting age for dependent children
8 specified in the policy shall not limit or restrict coverage with respect to an
9 unmarried child who meets all of the following criteria:
10 (A) is incapable of self-sustaining employment by reason of a mental

12 would qualify the child for benefits using the definitions, standards, and
13 methodology in 20 C.F.R. Part 404, Subpart P;
14 (B) became so incapable prior to attainment of the limiting age; and
15 (C) is chiefly dependent upon the employee, member, subscriber, or
16 policyholder for support and maintenance.
17 (2) Coverage under subdivision (1) of this subsection shall not be denied
18 any person based upon the existence of such a condition; provided, however,
19 that a health insurance plan may require reasonable periodic proof of a
20 continuing condition not more frequently than once every year.

10 § 4058. MEDICAL SUPPORT ORDERS
11 (a) As used in this section:
12 (1) “Dependent coverage” means family coverage, or coverage for one
13 or more persons as long as the coverage for one or more persons is greater than

20 on the grounds that:
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 83 of 181
1 (1) the child was born to unmarried parents;
2 (2) the child is not claimed as a dependent on the parent’s federal tax
3 return; or
4 (3) the child does not reside with the parent or in the health insurer’s
5 service area.

10 eligible for the coverage without regard to any enrollment season restrictions

13 Medicaid program, any State agency administering health benefits or a health

15 enforcement program.

17 insurer is provided satisfactory written evidence that:

21 date of disenrollment; or

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 84 of 181
1 (C) the employer has eliminated dependent health coverage for all of

1 of mailing, if the notice is mailed, or the date of actual receipt if another

14 (a) As used in this section, “covered individual” includes a member of a

17 this section.
18 (b) A covered individual who has exhausted all applicable internal review
19 procedures provided by the health insurance plan shall have the right to an
20 independent external review of a decision under a health insurance plan to
21 deny, reduce, or terminate health care coverage or to deny payment for a health
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 87 of 181
1 care service. The independent review shall be available when requested in
2 writing by the affected covered individual, provided the decision to be
3 reviewed requires the plan to expend at least $100.00 for the service and the
4 decision by the plan is based on one of the following reasons:
5 (1) The health care service is a covered benefit that the health insurer
6 has determined to be not medically necessary.
7 (2) A limitation is placed on the selection of a health care provider that
8 is claimed by the covered individual to be inconsistent with limits imposed by
9 the health insurance plan and any applicable laws and rules.
10 (3) The health care treatment has been determined to be experimental or
11 investigational or is an off-label drug. A health insurance plan that denies use
12 of a prescription drug for the treatment of cancer as not medically necessary or
13 as an experimental or investigational use shall treat any internal appeal of such
14 denial as an emergency or urgent appeal and shall decide the appeal within the
15 time frames applicable to emergency and urgent internal appeals under rules
16 adopted by the Commissioner.
17 (4) The health care service involves a medically based decision that a
18 condition is preexisting.
19 (5) The decision involves an adverse determination related to surprise
20 medical billing, as established under Section 2799A-1 or 2799A-2 of the
21 Public Health Service Act, including with respect to whether an item or service
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 88 of 181
1 that is the subject of the adverse determination is an item or service to which

5 the terms of coverage under a health insurance plan.
6 (d) The Department shall adopt rules necessary to carry out the purposes of
7 this section. The rules shall ensure that the independent external reviews have
8 the following characteristics:
9 (1) The independent external reviews shall be conducted:
10 (A) by independent review organizations pursuant to a contract with

20 (A) Be provided with adequate notice of the covered individual’s
21 review rights under this section.

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 89 of 181
1 (B) Have the right to use outside assistance during the review process

11 § 4064. MENTAL HEALTH SERVICES REVIEW
12 (a) The purposes of this section are to:
13 (1) promote the delivery of quality mental health services in a cost-
14 effective manner;
15 (2) foster the practice of mental health services review as a professional
16 collaborative process, the primary objective of which is to enhance the
17 effectiveness of clinical treatment;
18 (3) protect clients and patients, employers, and mental health providers
19 by ensuring that review agents are qualified to perform service review
20 activities and to make informed decisions on the appropriateness of mental
21 health care; and
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 91 of 181
1 (4) ensure the confidentiality of clients’ and patients’ mental health
2 records in the performance of service review activities in accordance with
3 applicable State and federal laws.
4 (b) Definitions. As used in this section:
5 (1) “License” means a review agent’s license granted by the
6 Commissioner.
7 (2) “Mental health provider” means any individual, corporation, facility,
8 or institution certified or licensed by this State to provide mental health
9 services, including a physician, nurse with recognized psychiatric specialties,
10 hospital or other health care facility, psychologist, clinical social worker,
11 mental health counselor, alcohol or drug abuse counselor, or an employee or
12 agent of such mental health provider acting in the course and scope of
13 employment or an agency related to mental health services.
14 (3) “Mental health services” mean acts of diagnosis, treatment,
15 evaluation, or advice or any other acts permissible under the health care laws
16 of Vermont, whether performed in an outpatient or institutional setting, and
17 include treatment for substance use disorder.
18 (4) “Review agent” means a person or entity performing service review

3 Subchapter 9. Required Covered Benefits
4 § 4067. APPLICATION OF SUBCHAPTER
5 (a) Unless otherwise specified and to the extent not inconsistent with
6 federal law, the benefits required in this subchapter:
7 (1) apply only to major medical insurance plans;
8 (2) may be subject to deductibles, co-payment and coinsurance amounts,
9 fee or benefit limits, practice parameters, and utilization review consistent with
10 any applicable rules and guidance adopted by the Department of Financial
11 Regulation; and
12 (3) do not apply to Vermont Medicaid.
13 (b) A health insurer may require benefits mandated in this subchapter to be
14 provided by a licensed health care provider under contract with the health
15 insurer; provided, however, that this provision shall not be construed to relieve
16 a health insurance plan from complying with the applicable network adequacy
17 requirements adopted by the Commissioner by rule.
18 § 4068. CHIROPRACTIC SERVICES
19 (a) A health insurance plan shall provide coverage for clinically necessary
20 health care services provided by a chiropractic physician licensed in this State
21 for treatment within the scope of practice described in 26 V.S.A. chapter 10,
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 97 of 181
1 but limiting adjunctive therapies to physiotherapy modalities and rehabilitative
2 exercises. A health insurance plan does not have to provide coverage for the
3 treatment of any visceral condition arising from problems or dysfunctions of
4 the abdominal or thoracic organs.
5 (b) A health insurer may require that the chiropractic services be
6 provided upon referral from a health care provider under contract with the
7 health insurer.
8 (c) For silver- and bronze-level qualified health benefit plans and any
9 reflective health benefit plans offered at the silver or bronze level pursuant to
10 33 V.S.A. chapter 18, subchapter 1, health care services provided by a
11 chiropractic physician may be subject to a co-payment requirement, provided
12 that any required co-payment amount shall be between 125 and 150 percent of
13 the amount of the co-payment applicable to care and services provided by a
14 primary care provider under the plan.
15 (d) Nothing in this section shall be construed as impeding or preventing
16 either the provision or coverage of health care services by licensed chiropractic
17 physicians, within the lawful scope of chiropractic practice, in hospital
18 facilities on a staff or employee basis.
19 § 4069. PROSTHETIC DEVICES
20 (a) As used in this section, “prosthetic device” means an artificial limb
21 device to replace, in whole or in part, an arm or a leg.
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 98 of 181
1 (b) A health insurance plan shall provide coverage for prosthetic devices
2 that is at least equivalent to the coverage provided by the federal Medicare
3 program. Coverage may be limited to the prosthetic device that is the most
4 appropriate model that is medically necessary to meet the patient’s medical
5 needs. Any dispute between the covered individual and the carrier concerning
6 coverage and the application of this section shall be subject to independent
7 external review under section 4063 of this title.
8 (c) A health insurance plan may require prior authorization for prosthetic
9 devices in the same manner and to the same extent as prior authorization is
10 required for any other covered benefit.
11 (d) A health insurance plan shall provide coverage under this section for
12 the medically necessary repair or replacement of a prosthetic device.
13 (e) The coverage for prosthetic devices shall not be subject to a deductible,
14 co-payment, or coinsurance provision that is less favorable to a covered
15 individual than the deductible, co-payment, or coinsurance provisions that
16 apply generally to other nonprimary care items and services under the health
17 insurance plan.

VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 99 of 181
1 (a) As used in this section:
2 (1) “Hearing aid” means any small, wearable electronic instrument or
3 device designed and intended for the ear for the purpose of aiding or
4 compensating for impaired human hearing and any related parts, attachments,
5 or accessories, including earmolds and associated remote microphones that
6 pair with hearing aids to improve word comprehension in difficult listening

9 auditoriums, or stand-alone assisted listening devices that can function without
10 a hearing aid.
11 (2) “Hearing aid professional services” means the practice of fitting,
12 selecting, dispensing, selling, or servicing hearing aids, or a combination,
13 including:
14 (A) evaluation for a hearing aid;
15 (B) fitting of a hearing aid;
16 (C) programming of a hearing aid;
17 (D) hearing aid repairs;
18 (E) follow-up adjustments, servicing, and maintenance of a hearing
19 aid;
20 (F) ear mold impressions; and
21 (G) auditory rehabilitation and training.
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 100 of 181
1 (3) “Hearing care professional” means an audiologist or hearing aid

3 26 V.S.A. chapter 23 or 33, a physician assistant licensed under 26 V.S.A.
4 chapter 31, or an advanced practice registered nurse licensed under 26 V.S.A.
5 chapter 28, working within that professional’s scope of practice.
6 (4) “Large group health insurance plan” means a major medical
7 insurance plan that meets the requirements of section 4041 of this title but that
8 is not:
9 (A) a qualified health benefit plan or reflective health benefit plan

12 association to one or more entities providing educational services pursuant to
13 24 V.S.A. chapter 121, subchapter 6.
14 (b)(1) A large group health insurance plan shall cover the cost of a hearing
15 aid for each ear and the associated hearing aid professional services when the

17 professional. The coverage shall include hearing aid batteries when prescribed
18 by a hearing care professional.

20 than one hearing aid per ear every three years, except that a plan shall cover
21 the cost of one or more new hearing aids for a covered individual prior to the
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 101 of 181
1 expiration of the three-year period based on a hearing care professional’s

3 necessary.
4 (c)(1) Subject to the limitations set forth in subdivision (b)(2) of this
5 section, the coverage provided by a large group health insurance plan for
6 hearing aids and associated services shall be limited only by medical necessity.
7 (2) A covered individual may select a hearing aid that exceeds the limits
8 set forth in subdivision (1) of this subsection and pay the additional cost.
9 (d) The coverage required by this section shall not be subject to a
10 deductible, co-payment, or coinsurance provision that is less favorable to a
11 covered individual than the deductible, co-payment, or coinsurance provisions
12 that apply generally to other nonprimary care items and services under the

7 coinsurance, co-payment, deductible, or other cost-sharing requirements for

16 § 4072. MENTAL HEALTH AND SUBSTANCE USE DISORDER
17 SERVICES
18 (a) It is the goal of the General Assembly that treatment for mental
19 conditions be recognized as an integral component of health care, that health
20 insurance plans cover all necessary and appropriate medical services without
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 103 of 181
1 imposing practices that create barriers to receiving appropriate care, and that

3 (b) As used in this section:
4 (1) “Mental condition” means any condition or disorder involving
5 psychiatric disabilities or substance use disorder that falls under any of the
6 diagnostic categories listed in the mental disorders section of the International
7 Classification of Diseases, as periodically revised.
8 (2) “Mental health provider” means any individual, corporation, facility,
9 or institution certified or licensed by this State to provide mental health
10 services, including a physician, nurse with recognized psychiatric specialties,
11 hospital or other health care facility, psychologist, clinical social worker,
12 mental health counselor, alcohol or drug abuse counselor, or an employee or
13 agent of such provider acting in the course and scope of employment or an
14 agency related to mental health services.
15 (3) “Rate, term, or condition” means any lifetime or annual payment
16 limits, deductibles, copayments, coinsurance, and any other cost-sharing
17 requirements, out-of-pocket limits, visit limits, and any other financial
18 component of health insurance coverage that affects the covered individual.

20 condition and shall:
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 104 of 181

5 applicable to care or services provided by a primary care provider under a
6 covered individual’s health insurance plan and no greater co-payment for
7 specialty mental health care or services than the co-payment applicable to care
8 or services provided by a specialist provider under a covered individual’s
9 health insurance plan;
10 (2) not exclude from its network or list of authorized providers any
11 licensed mental health or substance use disorder treatment provider located
12 within the geographic coverage area of the health insurance plan if the provider

7 § 4074. TREATMENT OF INHERITED METABOLIC DISORDERS
8 (a) As used in this section:
9 (1) “Inherited metabolic disorder” means a disorder caused by an
10 inherited abnormality of body chemistry for which the State screens newborn
11 infants.
12 (2) “Low protein modified food product” means a food product that is
13 specifically formulated to have less than one gram of protein per serving and is
14 intended to be used under the direction of a health care professional for the
15 dietary treatment of a metabolic disorder.
16 (3) “Medical food” means an amino acid modified preparation that is
17 intended to be used under the direction of a health care professional for the
18 dietary treatment of an inherited metabolic disorder.
19 (b) A health insurance plan shall provide coverage for medical foods
20 prescribed for medically necessary treatment for an inherited metabolic
21 disorder.
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 112 of 181
1 (c) Coverage for low protein modified food products prescribed for
2 medically necessary treatment of an inherited metabolic disorder shall be at
3 least $2,500.00 during any continuous period of 12 months for any covered
4 individual.
5 § 4075. CRANIOFACIAL DISORDERS
6 (a)(1) A health insurance plan shall provide coverage for diagnosis and
7 medically necessary treatment, including surgical and nonsurgical procedures,
8 for a musculoskeletal disorder that affects any bone or joint in the face, neck,
9 or head and is the result of accident, trauma, congenital defect, developmental
10 defect, or pathology. Subject to subsection (b) of this section, this coverage
11 shall be the same as that provided under the health insurance plan for any other
12 musculoskeletal disorder in the body and shall be covered when the diagnosis
13 or treatment, or both, is prescribed or administered by a physician or a dentist.
14 (2) This section shall not be construed to require coverage for dental
15 services for the diagnosis or treatment of dental disorders or dental pathology
16 primarily affecting the gums, teeth, or alveolar ridge.
17 (b) A health insurance plan may require a referral from a health care
18 provider under contract with the plan.

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 113 of 181
1 § 4076. HOME HEALTH SERVICES
2 (a) As used in this section:
3 (1) “ Home health agency” means a nonprofit home health agency that
4 has been certified under Title XVIII of the Social Security Act (42 U.S.C.
5 § 1395 et seq.).
6 (2) “Home health care” means care and treatment provided by a home
7 health agency and designed and supervised by a health care professional,
8 without which care and treatment a person would require admission to a
9 hospital or skilled nursing facility, as those terms are defined by Medicare
10 regulations. The care and treatment shall consist of one or more of the
11 following:
12 (A) Part-time or intermittent skilled nursing care.
13 (B) Physical therapy.
14 (C) Part-time or intermittent home health aide services that consist
15 primarily of caring for the patient.
16 (D) Medical supplies, drugs and equipment, and laboratory services
17 to the extent that laboratory services would have been covered if the patient
18 had been admitted to a hospital or skilled nursing facility. The medical
19 necessity of equipment may be reviewed by reference to the Medicare
20 guidelines for durable medical equipment.
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 114 of 181
1 (b)(1) A major medical insurance plan shall provide coverage for home
2 health care.
3 (2) A health insurer may require evidence of insurability as a
4 prerequisite to coverage.
5 (3) The coverage shall consist of at least 40 visits by a home health
6 agency in any calendar year, or in any continuous period of 12 months, for
7 each person covered under the health insurance plan.
8 (4) Each visit by a member of a home health care agency, other than a
9 home health aide, shall be considered one home health care visit, and four
10 hours of home health aide service shall be considered one home health care
11 visit. Coverage shall be provided for maternity and childbirth.
12 (c) Nothing in this section shall be deemed to require that home health care
13 coverage be provided to individuals eligible for Medicare.
14 (d) A health insurance plan shall not impose greater coinsurance, co-
15 payment, deductible, or other cost-sharing requirements for coverage of home
16 health care than apply to the diagnosis and treatment of any other physical or
17 mental condition under the plan.
18 § 4077. REPRODUCTIVE HEALTH CARE SERVICES
19 (a)(1) A health insurance plan shall provide coverage for outpatient
20 contraceptive services including sterilizations, and shall provide coverage for
21 the purchase of all prescription contraceptives and prescription contraceptive
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 115 of 181
1 devices approved by the U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA), except
2 that a health insurance plan that does not provide coverage of prescription
3 drugs is not required to provide coverage of prescription contraceptives and

5 (2) A health insurance plan providing coverage required under this
6 section shall not establish any rate, term, or condition that places a greater
7 financial burden on a covered individual for access to contraceptive services,
8 prescription contraceptives, and prescription contraceptive devices than for

15 (1) The coverage provided pursuant to this subsection shall include

5 § 4080. ANESTHESIA FOR CERTAIN DENTAL PROCEDURES
6 (a) As used in this section:

5 § 4081. TOBACCO CESSATION
6 (a) As used in this section, “tobacco cessation medication” means all

14 tobacco cessation medication.

VT LEG #382889 v.1

3 § 4083. SERVICES FOR VICTIMS OF SEXUAL ASSAULT
4 (a) As used in this section, “sexual assault examination” means either or
5 both of the following:
6 (1) a physical examination of the patient, documentation of biological
7 and physical findings, and collection of evidence; and
8 (2) treatment of the patient’s injuries; providing care for sexually
9 transmitted infections; assessing pregnancy risk; discussing treatment options,
10 including reproductive health services, screening for the human
11 immunodeficiency virus, and prophylactic treatment when appropriate; and
12 providing instructions and referrals for follow-up care.

15 cost-sharing requirement for the sexual assault examination of a victim of
16 alleged sexual assault for health care services associated with specific
17 procedure codes identified in a memorandum of understanding between the
18 health insurer and the Vermont Center for Crime Victim Services.

6 Subchapter 10. Prescription Drug Coverage
7 § 4091. DEFINITIONS
8 As used in this subchapter:

13 pharmacy provider’s services.

16 physician assistant under 26 V.S.A. chapter 31, or an individual licensed as an
17 advanced practice registered nurse under 26 V.S.A. chapter 28.

19 this chapter and includes prescription drug benefits managed by a health

3 (5) “Out-of-pocket expenditure” means a co-payment, coinsurance,
4 deductible, or other cost-sharing mechanism.
5 (6) “Pharmacy benefit manager” means an entity that performs
6 pharmacy benefit management. “Pharmacy benefit management” means an
7 arrangement for the procurement of prescription drugs at negotiated dispensing
8 rates, the administration or management of prescription drug benefits provided

VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30

15 (10) “Step therapy” means protocols that establish the specific sequence

9 § 4093. RETAIL PHARMACIES; FILLING OF PRESCRIPTIONS
10 (a) A health insurer or pharmacy benefit manager doing business in

13 same level of reimbursement as they are filled by any other pharmacist or
14 pharmacy, including a mail-order pharmacy or a pharmacy benefit manager
15 affiliate, with respect to the quantity of drugs or days’ supply of drugs
16 dispensed under each prescription.
17 (b) Notwithstanding any provision of a health insurance plan to the
18 contrary, if a health insurance plan provides for payment or reimbursement that
19 is within the lawful scope of practice of a pharmacist, the health insurer may
20 provide payment or reimbursement for the service when the service is provided
21 by a pharmacist.

15 Subchapter 11. Prevention and Treatment of Cancer
16 § 4095a. COLORECTAL CANCER SCREENING
17 (a) As used in this section, “colonoscopy” means a procedure that enables
18 a health care professional to examine visually the inside of a patient’s entire
19 colon and includes the concurrent removal of polyps or biopsy, or both.
20 (b) A health insurance plan shall provide coverage for colorectal cancer
21 screening, including:
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 142 of 181
1 (1) for a covered individual who is not at high risk for colorectal cancer,
2 colorectal cancer screening examinations and laboratory tests in accordance
3 with the most recently published recommendations established by the U.S.
4 Preventive Services Task Force for average-risk individuals; and
5 (2) for a covered individual who is at high risk for colorectal cancer,
6 colorectal cancer screening examinations and laboratory tests as recommended
7 by the treating health care professional.
8 (c) For the purposes of subdivision (b)(2) of this section, an individual is at
9 high risk for colorectal cancer if the individual has:
10 (1) a family medical history of colorectal cancer or a genetic syndrome
11 predisposing the individual to colorectal cancer;
12 (2) a prior occurrence of colorectal cancer or precursor polyps;
13 (3) a prior occurrence of a chronic digestive disease condition such as
14 inflammatory bowel disease, Crohn’s disease, or ulcerative colitis; or
15 (4) other predisposing factors as determined by the individual’s treating
16 health care professional.
17 (d) Colorectal cancer screening services performed under contract with the
18 insurer shall not be subject to any co-payment, deductible, coinsurance, or
19 other cost-sharing requirement. In addition, a covered individual shall not be
20 subject to any additional charge for any service associated with a procedure or
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 143 of 181
1 test for colorectal cancer screening, which may include one or more of the
2 following:
3 (1) removal of tissue or other matter;
4 (2) laboratory services;
5 (3) health care professional services;
6 (4) facility use; and
7 (5) anesthesia.
8 § 4095b. MAMMOGRAPHY AND OTHER BREAST IMAGING
9 SERVICES
10 (a)(1) A health insurance plan shall provide coverage for screening
11 mammography and for other medically necessary breast imaging services upon
12 recommendation of a health care professional as needed to detect the presence
13 of breast cancer and other abnormalities of the breast or breast tissue. In
14 addition, a health insurance plan shall provide coverage for screening by
15 ultrasound or another appropriate imaging service for a covered individual for
16 whom the results of a screening mammogram were inconclusive or who has
17 dense breast tissue, or both.
18 (2) Benefits provided shall cover the full cost of the mammography,
19 ultrasound, and other breast imaging services and shall not be subject to any
20 co-payment, deductible, coinsurance, or other cost-sharing requirement or
21 additional charge, except to the extent that such coverage would disqualify a
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 144 of 181
1 high-deductible health plan from eligibility for a health savings account
2 pursuant to 26 U.S.C. § 223.
3 (b) This section shall apply only to procedures conducted by test facilities
4 accredited by the American College of Radiologists.
5 (c) As used in this section:
6 (1) “Mammography” means the x-ray examination of the breast using
7 equipment dedicated specifically for mammography, including the x-ray tube,
8 filter, compression device, and digital detector. The term includes breast
9 tomosynthesis.
10 (2) “Other breast imaging services” means diagnostic mammography,
11 ultrasound, and magnetic resonance imaging services that enable health care
12 professionals to detect the presence or absence of breast cancer and other
13 abnormalities affecting the breast or breast tissue.
14 (3) “Screening” includes the mammography or ultrasound test procedure
15 and a qualified health care professional’s interpretation of the results of the
16 procedure, including additional views and interpretation as needed.

3 § 4095d. CHEMOTHERAPY TREATMENT AND ORAL ANTICANCER
4 MEDICATIONS
5 (a) A health insurance plan shall provide coverage for medically necessary

10 cancerous cells that is not less favorable on a financial basis than intravenously
11 administered or injected anticancer medications covered under the covered

15 § 4095f. OFF-LABEL USE OF PRESCRIPTION DRUGS FOR CANCER
16 (a) As used in this section:
17 (1) “Medical or scientific evidence” means one or more of the following
18 sources:
19 (A) peer-reviewed scientific studies published in or accepted for
20 publication by medical journals that meet nationally recognized requirements

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30

1 for scientific manuscripts and that submit most of their published articles for

5 National Library of Medicine for indexing in Index Medicus, Excerpta
6 Medicus (EMBASE), Medline, and MEDLARS database Health Services

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 149 of 181
1 (F) peer-reviewed abstracts accepted for presentation at major
2 medical association meetings.
3 (2) “Medically accepted indication” includes any use of a drug that has
4 been approved by the U.S. Food and Drug Administration and includes another
5 use of the drug if that use is prescribed by the covered individual’s health care
6 professional and supported by medical or scientific evidence.
7 (3) “Off-label use” means the prescription and use of drugs for
8 medically accepted indications other than those stated in the labeling approved
9 by the U.S. Food and Drug Administration.
10 (b) A health insurance plan shall provide coverage for off-label use in
11 cancer treatment in accordance with the following:
12 (1) A health insurance plan contract shall not exclude coverage for any
13 drug used for the treatment of cancer on grounds that the drug has not been
14 approved by the U.S. Food and Drug Administration, provided the use of the
15 drug is a medically accepted indication for the treatment of cancer.
16 (2) Coverage of a drug required by this section also includes medically
17 necessary services associated with the administration of the drug.
18 (3) This section shall not be construed to require coverage for a drug
19 when the U.S. Food and Drug Administration has determined its use to be
20 contraindicated for treatment of the current indication.
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 150 of 181
1 (4) A drug use that is covered under subdivision (1) of this subsection
2 shall not be denied coverage based on a “medical necessity” requirement
3 except for a reason unrelated to the legal status of the drug use.
4 (5) A health insurance plan that provides coverage of a drug as required
5 by this section may contain provisions for maximum benefits and coinsurance
6 and reasonable limitations, deductibles, and exclusions to the same extent these
7 provisions are applicable to coverage of all prescription drugs and are not
8 inconsistent with the requirements of this section.
9 (c) A determination by a health insurer that an off-label use of a

13 (d) This section shall apply to Medicaid and any other public health care

1 (a) As used in this section:

7 (3) “Health care facility” has the same meaning as in 18 V.S.A. § 9402.

16 office, a hospital, or a health care facility, or the patient’s home or another

18 based health center, or the patient’s workplace.
19 (6) “Store-and-forward” means an asynchronous transmission of

VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30

4 by a health care provider at a distant site who is trained in the relevant
5 specialty. In store-and-forward, the health care provider at the distant site
6 reviews the medical information without the patient present in real time and
7 communicates a care plan or treatment recommendation back to the patient or
8 referring provider, or both.
9 (7) “Telemedicine” means the delivery of health care services, including

13 1996, Pub. L. No. 104-191.
14 (b)(1) A health insurance plan shall provide coverage for health care
15 services and dental services delivered through telemedicine by a health care

17 same extent that the plan would cover the services if they were provided
18 through in-person consultation.
19 (2)(A) A health insurance plan shall provide the same reimbursement
20 rate for services billed using equivalent procedure codes and modifiers, subject
21 to the terms of the health insurance plan and provider contract, regardless of
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 153 of 181
1 whether the service was provided through an in-person visit with the health

9 and medical eye care services that are within the lawful scope of practice of the

18 condition or requirement for the optometrist’s or ophthalmologist’s
19 participation as a provider in any health insurance or vision care plan or
20 contract.

14 * * * Interpretation and Rule Alignment * * *
15 Sec. 32. INTERPRETATION; RULE ALIGNMENT
16 (a) The purpose of this bill is to update and reorganize the health insurance
17 statutes. It is the intent of the General Assembly that the technical
18 amendments in this act shall not supersede substantive changes contained in
19 other bills enacted by the General Assembly during the current biennium.
20 Where possible, the amendments in this act shall be interpreted to be
21 supplemental to other amendments made to the sections of 8 V.S.A. chapter
VT LEG #382889 v.1

AS PASSED BY HOUSE AND SENATE S.30
2025 Page 181 of 181
1 107 using the numbering scheme in effect prior to the effective date of this act;
2 to the extent the provisions conflict, the substantive changes in other acts shall
3 take precedence over the technical changes in this act. Statutes added to or
4 amended in 8 V.S.A. chapter 107 that are enacted during the 2025–2026
5 biennium using the numbering scheme that existed prior to the effective date of
6 this act shall be codified in the corresponding statutes as renumbered by this
7 act.
8 (b) Rules adopted and orders, bulletins, forms, and guidance documents
9 issued by the Department of Financial Regulation, the Green Mountain Care
10 Board, and other State agencies that refer to statutes in 8 V.S.A. chapter 107
11 using the numbering that existed prior to the effective date of this act shall
12 continue to be valid following the effective date of this act until such time as
13 the relevant documents can be amended or updated to align with the
14 renumbering of that chapter by this act.
15 * * * Effective Date * * *
16 Sec. 33. EFFECTIVE DATE
17 This act shall take effect on September 1, 2025.
